.hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico,_history" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of Ponce, Puerto Rico, history">Timeline of Ponce, Puerto Rico, history</a></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places_listings_in_southern_Puerto_Rico#Ponce" title="National Register of Historic Places listings in southern Puerto Rico">National Register of Historic Places listings in southern Puerto Rico \xc2\xa7&#160;Ponce</a></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Early_settlers">Early settlers</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early settlers"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The region of what is now Ponce belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> <a href="/wiki/Guaynia" title="Guaynia">Guaynia</a> region, which stretched along the southern coast of Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ag%C3%BCeyban%C3%A1_I" title="Ag\xc3\xbceyban\xc3\xa1 I">Ag\xc3\xbceyban\xc3\xa1</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">cacique</a> who led the region, was among those who greeted Spanish conquistador <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n">Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n</a> when he came to the island in 1508. Archaeological findings have identified four sites within the municipality of Ponce with archaeological significance: <a href="/wiki/Canas_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Canas (Ponce)">Canas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tibes_Indigenous_Ceremonial_Center" title="Tibes Indigenous Ceremonial Center">Tibes</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Ant%C3%B3n" title="San Ant\xc3\xb3n">Caracoles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sabanetas_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sabanetas (Ponce)">El Bronce</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>During the first years of the <a href="/wiki/Colonization" title="Colonization">colonization</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish people">Spanish</a> families started settling around the <a href="/wiki/Jacaguas_River" title="Jacaguas River">Jacaguas River</a>, in the south of the island.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> For security reasons,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> these families moved to the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Portugu%C3%A9s" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio Portugu\xc3\xa9s">Rio Portugu\xc3\xa9s</a>, then called Baramaya.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Starting around 1646 the whole area from the Rio Portugu\xc3\xa9s to the Bay of <a href="/wiki/Guayanilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Guayanilla">Guayanilla</a> was called Ponce.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1670, a small <a href="/wiki/Chapel" title="Chapel">chapel</a> was raised in the middle of the small settlement and dedicated in honor of <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Guadalupe" title="Our Lady of Guadalupe">Our Lady of Guadalupe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Among its earliest settlers were <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ponce_de_Le%C3%B3n_y_Loayza" title="Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n y Loayza">Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n y Loayza</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> Don Pedro Rodr\xc3\xadguez de Guzm\xc3\xa1n, from nearby <a href="/wiki/San_Germ%C3%A1n" class="mw-redirect" title="San Germ\xc3\xa1n">San Germ\xc3\xa1n</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On September 17, 1692, the King of Spain <a href="/wiki/Carlos_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlos II">Carlos II</a> issued a <i>C\xc3\xa9dula Real</i> (Royal Permit) converting the chapel into a parish, and in so doing officially recognizing the small settlement as a hamlet.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is believed that Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n y Loayza, Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n\'s great-grandson, was instrumental in obtaining the royal permit to formalize the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Hamlet_(place)" title="Hamlet (place)">hamlet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Captains Enrique Salazar and Miguel del Toro were also instrumental.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The city is named after Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n y Loayza,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the great-grandson of Spanish conquistador Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In the early 18th century Don Antonio Abad Rodriguez Berrios built a small chapel under the name of San Antonio Abad. The area would later receive the name of <i><a href="/wiki/San_Ant%C3%B3n" title="San Ant\xc3\xb3n">San Ant\xc3\xb3n</a></i>, a historically important part of modern Ponce.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1712 the village was chartered as <i>El Poblado de Nuestra Se\xc3\xb1ora de Guadalupe de Ponce</i> (The Village of Our Lady of Guadalupe of Ponce).<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="19th-century_immigrants">19th-century immigrants</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 19th-century immigrants"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>In the early 19th century, Ponce continued to be one of dozens of hamlets that dotted the Island. Its inhabitants survived by <a href="/wiki/Subsistence_agriculture" title="Subsistence agriculture">subsistence agriculture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cattle_raising" class="mw-redirect" title="Cattle raising">cattle raising</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sea" title="Sea">maritime</a> <a href="/wiki/Contraband" title="Contraband">contraband</a> with foreigners. Mayor <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ben%C3%ADtez_(mayor)" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Ben\xc3\xadtez (mayor)">Jos\xc3\xa9 Ben\xc3\xadtez</a> categorized the jurisdiction into <i>cotos</i>, <i>hatos</i>, <i>criaderos</i>, <i>monter\xc3\xadas</i>, and <i>terrenos realengos</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i>Cotos</i> were lands awarded to residents as reward for their services to the king. They were developed into <a href="/wiki/Estancias" class="mw-redirect" title="Estancias">estancias</a> or lands apt to be cultivated for agricultural use. <i>Hatos</i> were lands not granted to anyone in particular, but available for communal use where cattle could roam at will. <i>Monter\xc3\xadas</i> were hilly areas located next to <i>hatos</i> were cattle could be reigned in or gathered together with the help of trained dogs. <i>Criaderos</i> were lands were cows could be herded for milk production. Goats, sheep, pigs, asses, and mares were also herded in <i>criaderos</i>. <i>Terrenos realengos</i> were lands that belonged to the state (to the king).<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>However, in the 1820s, three events dramatically changed the size of the town. The first of these events was the arrival of a significant number of white <a href="/wiki/Geographical_distribution_of_French_speakers" title="Geographical distribution of French speakers">Francophones</a>, fleeing the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">Haitian Revolution</a> of 1791\xe2\x80\x931804.<sup id="cite_ref-Eduardo_Neumann_Gandia_1913._p._38_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eduardo_Neumann_Gandia_1913._p._38-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The effect of this mass migration was not felt significantly until the 1820s. These French Creole <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneurs" class="mw-redirect" title="Entrepreneurs">entrepreneurs</a> were attracted to the area because of its large flatlands, and they came with enough capital, <a href="/wiki/Slaves" class="mw-redirect" title="Slaves">slaves</a>, and commercial connections to stimulate Ponce\'s <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a> production and sales.<sup id="cite_ref-Figueroa_2006_p._58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Figueroa_2006_p.-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Secondly, <a href="/wiki/Landlords" class="mw-redirect" title="Landlords">landlords</a> and <a href="/wiki/Merchants" class="mw-redirect" title="Merchants">merchants</a> migrated from various Latin American countries. They had migrated for better conditions, as they were leaving economic decline following the revolutions and disruption of societies as nations gained independence from Spain in the 1810s-1820s.<sup id="cite_ref-Eduardo_Neumann_Gandia_1913._p._38_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eduardo_Neumann_Gandia_1913._p._38-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Third, the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Royal_Decree_of_Graces_of_1815" title="Royal Decree of Graces of 1815">Royal Decree of Graces of 1815</a> attracted numerous European immigrants to Puerto Rico. It encouraged any citizen of a country politically friendly to Spain to settle in Puerto Rico as long as they converted to the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> faith and agreed to work in the <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agricultural</a> business. With such mass migrations, not only the size of the town was changed, but the character of its population was changed as well. Europeans, including many <a href="/wiki/Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestants">Protestants</a>, immigrated from a variety of nations.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On July 29, 1848, and as a result of this explosive growth, the Ponce hamlet was declared a <i>villa</i> (village) by <a href="/wiki/Queen_Isabella_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Isabella II">Queen Isabella II</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and in 1877 the village obtained its city charter.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Complejo_Museo_Hacienda_Buena_Vista,_mirando_al_sur,_desde_la_Depulpadora_de_Cafe,_en_Bo._Magueyes,_Ponce,_PR_(DSC03604).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Complejo_Museo_Hacienda_Buena_Vista%2C_mirando_al_sur%2C_desde_la_Depulpadora_de_Cafe%2C_en_Bo._Magueyes%2C_Ponce%2C_PR_%28DSC03604%29.jpg/200px-Complejo_Museo_Hacienda_Buena_Vista%2C_mirando_al_sur%2C_desde_la_Depulpadora_de_Cafe%2C_en_Bo._Magueyes%2C_Ponce%2C_PR_%28DSC03604%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Complejo_Museo_Hacienda_Buena_Vista%2C_mirando_al_sur%2C_desde_la_Depulpadora_de_Cafe%2C_en_Bo._Magueyes%2C_Ponce%2C_PR_%28DSC03604%29.jpg/300px-Complejo_Museo_Hacienda_Buena_Vista%2C_mirando_al_sur%2C_desde_la_Depulpadora_de_Cafe%2C_en_Bo._Magueyes%2C_Ponce%2C_PR_%28DSC03604%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Complejo_Museo_Hacienda_Buena_Vista%2C_mirando_al_sur%2C_desde_la_Depulpadora_de_Cafe%2C_en_Bo._Magueyes%2C_Ponce%2C_PR_%28DSC03604%29.jpg/400px-Complejo_Museo_Hacienda_Buena_Vista%2C_mirando_al_sur%2C_desde_la_Depulpadora_de_Cafe%2C_en_Bo._Magueyes%2C_Ponce%2C_PR_%28DSC03604%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a><figcaption>Many mid-18th-century immigrants made fortunes in Ponce, like the owner of this restored coffee plantation (<a href="/wiki/Hacienda_Buena_Vista" title="Hacienda Buena Vista">Hacienda Buena Vista</a>) founded in 1833; today it is a point of interest in the municipality</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Some of these immigrants made considerable fortunes in <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a> and sugarcane harvesting, <a href="/wiki/Rum" title="Rum">rum</a> production,<sup id="cite_ref-Pedro_Tom\xc3\xa1s_de_C\xc3\xb3rdova_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pedro_Tom\xc3\xa1s_de_C\xc3\xb3rdova-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bank" title="Bank">banking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Finance" title="Finance">finance</a>, the importing of industrial machinery, <a href="/wiki/Foundry" title="Foundry">iron foundries</a> and other enterprises. At the time of the American invasion of the Island in 1898, Ponce was a thriving city,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> boasting the Island\'s main financial center,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the Island\'s first communications link to another country,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the best capitalized financial institutions, and even its own currency.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It had consular offices for England, Germany, the Netherlands, and other nations.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Following trends set in Europe and elsewhere, in 1877, <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Rosich_y_Mass" class="mw-redirect" title="Miguel Rosich y Mass">Don Miguel Rosich</a> conceived an exposition for Ponce. This was approved in 1880, and the Ponce Fair was held in the city in 1882. It showed several industrial and agricultural advancements. \n</p>\n<blockquote><p>"It is important to establish a relationship between the European exhibitions that I have mentioned and the Ponce Fair, as the Fair was meant as a showcase of the advancements of the day: Agriculture, Trade, Industry, and the Arts. Just as with the <a href="/wiki/1878_World%27s_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="1878 World&#39;s Fair">1878 World\'s Fair</a> in Paris, the electric grid of the city of Ponce was inaugurated on the first day of the Ponce Fair. In this occasion the <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Las_Delicias" title="Plaza Las Delicias">Plaza Las Delicias</a> and various other buildings, including the Mercantile Union Building, the <a href="/wiki/Old_Ponce_Casino" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Ponce Casino">Ponce Casino</a>, and some of Ponce\'s homes were illuminated with the <a href="/wiki/Incandescent_light_bulb" title="Incandescent light bulb">incandescent light bulb</a> for the first time".<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Ponce_in_the_20th_century">Ponce in the 20th century</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ponce in the 20th century"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="U.S._invasion">U.S. invasion</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: U.S. invasion"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican Campaign">Puerto Rican Campaign</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:US_troopships_and_convoy_at_Playa_de_Ponce,_1898.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/US_troopships_and_convoy_at_Playa_de_Ponce%2C_1898.jpg/220px-US_troopships_and_convoy_at_Playa_de_Ponce%2C_1898.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/US_troopships_and_convoy_at_Playa_de_Ponce%2C_1898.jpg/330px-US_troopships_and_convoy_at_Playa_de_Ponce%2C_1898.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/US_troopships_and_convoy_at_Playa_de_Ponce%2C_1898.jpg/440px-US_troopships_and_convoy_at_Playa_de_Ponce%2C_1898.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1904" /></a><figcaption>The 1898 landing of U.S. troops at <a href="/wiki/Playa_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Playa (Ponce)">Playa de Ponce</a> led to a period economic stagnation for Ponce, as the Americans chose to centralize the administration of the island in San Juan</figcaption></figure>\n<p>At the time of the U.S. <a href="/wiki/History_of_Puerto_Rico#Invasion_of_1898" title="History of Puerto Rico">invasion and occupation of Puerto Rico in 1898</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War">Spanish\xe2\x80\x93American War</a>, Ponce was the largest city in the island with a population of 22,000. Ponce had the best road in Puerto Rico, running from Ponce to <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>, which had been built by the Spaniards for military purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The taking of Ponce by American troops "was a critical turning point in the Puerto Rican campaign. For the first time the Americans held a major port to funnel large numbers of men and quantities of war material into the island." Ponce also had underwater <a href="/wiki/Telegraph" class="mw-redirect" title="Telegraph">telegraph</a> cable connections with <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> and the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a>, putting the U.S. forces on the island in direct communication with <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, for the first time since the beginning of the campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Just prior to the United States occupation of the island, Ponce was a flourishing and dynamic city with a significant number of public facilities, a large number of industries and commercial firms, and a great number of exquisite residences that reflected the high standing of its bourgeoisie.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On July 27, American troops, aboard the <i><a href="/wiki/USS_Cincinnati_(C-7)" title="USS Cincinnati (C-7)">Cincinnati</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/USS_Dixie_(1893)" title="USS Dixie (1893)">Dixie</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/USS_Wasp_(1893)" title="USS Wasp (1893)"><i>Wasp</i></a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/USS_Gloucester_(1891)" title="USS Gloucester (1891)">Gloucester</a></i>, disembarked at Playa de Ponce.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> General Nelson Miles arrived the next day with reinforcements from <a href="/wiki/Gu%C3%A1nica,_Puerto_Rico" title="Gu\xc3\xa1nica, Puerto Rico">Gu\xc3\xa1nica</a> and took possession of the city. There were some minor skirmishes in the city, but no major battle was fought. Three men were killed and 13 wounded on the Spanish side, while the Americans suffered four wounded. The American flag was raised in the town center that same day and most of the Spanish troops retreated into the surrounding mountains. The U.S. Army then established its headquarters in Ponce.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Period_of_stagnation">Period of stagnation</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Period of stagnation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>After the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Puerto_Rico#Invasion_of_1898" title="History of Puerto Rico">U.S. invasion</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">Americans</a> chose to centralize the administration of the island in <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> the capital, neglecting the south and thus starting a period of socio-<a href="/wiki/Economic_stagnation" title="Economic stagnation">economic stagnation</a> for Ponce.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This was worsened by several factors:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/1899_Hurricane_San_Ciriaco" class="mw-redirect" title="1899 Hurricane San Ciriaco">Hurricane San Ciriaco</a> in 1899 had left the region in misery<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>The opening of sugar mills in <a href="/wiki/Salinas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Salinas, Puerto Rico">Salinas</a><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Gu%C3%A1nica,_Puerto_Rico" title="Gu\xc3\xa1nica, Puerto Rico">Gu\xc3\xa1nica</a><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> drew commercial and agricultural activity away from Ponce<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>The decadence in <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> plantations in the 1920s<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>The loss of the Spanish and <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuban</a> markets<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> "The Spanish American War had paralyzed the trade of the Island of Puerto Rico and when Spain surrendered the sovereignty she closed her [Spain\'s] ports to Puerto Rican products, while the American occupation of Cuba destroyed the only other important market. As a result, the trade in coffee and tobacco was ruined, and nothing was provided by the Americans to take their place."<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>At least one author has also blamed the stagnation on "the strife between the U.S. and the local <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Nationalist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican Nationalist Party">Nationalist Party</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The 20th century financial stagnation prompted residents to initiate measures to attract economic activity back into the city. Also, a solid manufacturing industry surged that still remains. Examples of this are the <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Cement,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Ponce Cement, Inc.">Ponce Cement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Iron_Works" title="Puerto Rico Iron Works">Puerto Rico Iron Works</a>, <a href="/wiki/Industrias_Vassallo" title="Industrias Vassallo">Vassallo Industries</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Destiler%C3%ADa_Serrall%C3%A9s" title="Destiler\xc3\xada Serrall\xc3\xa9s">Destiler\xc3\xada Serrall\xc3\xa9s</a>. <a href="/wiki/El_Nuevo_Dia" class="mw-redirect" title="El Nuevo Dia">El Dia</a> was also founded in Ponce in 1911.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Ponce_massacre">Ponce massacre</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Ponce massacre"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ponce_Massacre.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ponce_Massacre.JPG/250px-Ponce_Massacre.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="144" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ponce_Massacre.JPG/375px-Ponce_Massacre.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Ponce_Massacre.JPG/500px-Ponce_Massacre.JPG 2x" data-file-width="637" data-file-height="368" /></a><figcaption>Police fire upon unarmed <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Nationalist Party of Puerto Rico">Nationalists</a> killing 21 in what came to be known as the <a href="/wiki/Ponce_massacre" title="Ponce massacre">Ponce massacre</a> of 1937</figcaption></figure>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ponce_massacre" title="Ponce massacre">Ponce massacre</a></div>\n<p>On March 21, 1937, a peaceful march was organized by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Nationalist_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican Nationalist Party">Puerto Rican Nationalist Party</a> to celebrate the 64th anniversary of the abolition of slavery and protest the incarceration of their leader, Dr. <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Albizu_Campos" title="Pedro Albizu Campos">Pedro Albizu Campos</a>, in a federal prison on charges of <a href="/wiki/Sedition" title="Sedition">sedition</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-llmc.com_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-llmc.com-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The march turned into a bloody event when the Insular Police, a force somewhat resembling the <a href="/wiki/National_Guard_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="National Guard of the United States">National Guard</a> of the typical U.S. state and which answered to U.S.-appointed governor <a href="/wiki/Blanton_Winship" title="Blanton Winship">Blanton Winship</a>, opened fire on\nunarmed and defenseless members of the <a href="/wiki/Cadets_of_the_Republic" title="Cadets of the Republic">Cadets of the Republic</a> and bystanders.<sup id="cite_ref-llmc.com_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-llmc.com-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>When the shooting stopped, nineteen civilians had been killed or mortally wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Over two hundred others were badly wounded.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Many were shot in their backs while running away, including a seven-year-old girl named Georgina Maldonado who was "killed through the back while running to a nearby church."<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The US commissioned an independent investigation headed by Arthur Garfield Hays, general counsel of the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_Liberties_Union" title="American Civil Liberties Union">American Civil Liberties Union</a>, together with prominent citizens of Puerto Rico. The members concluded in their report that the event was a massacre, with the police acting as a mob. They harshly criticized Winship\'s actions as governor and said he had numerous abuses of civil rights.<sup id="cite_ref-Vito_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vito-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The event has since been known as the <a href="/wiki/Ponce_massacre" title="Ponce massacre">Ponce massacre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Vito_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vito-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was the largest massacre in Puerto Rican history.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As a result of this report and other charges against Winship, he was dismissed from his position in 1937 and replaced as governor.<sup id="cite_ref-Vito_95-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vito-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The history of this event can be viewed at the <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_la_Masacre_de_Ponce" title="Museo de la Masacre de Ponce">Ponce Massacre Museum</a> on Marina Street. An open-air park in the city, the <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Albizu_Campos_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedro Albizu Campos Park">Pedro Albizu Campos Park</a>, is dedicated to the memory of the president of the Puerto Rican Nationalist Party. As a result of this event, Ponce has been identified as "the birthplace of Puerto Rican national identity."<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ponce history in general is expressed at the <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_la_Historia_de_Ponce" title="Museo de la Historia de Ponce">Ponce History Museum</a>, on the block bordered by Isabel, Mayor, Cristina, and Salud streets in the historic downtown area.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Hub_for_political_and_economic_activity">Hub for political and economic activity</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Hub for political and economic activity"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Ponce has continued to be a hub of political activity on the island, and is the founding site of several major political parties. It has also been the birthplace of several important political figures of the island, including <a href="/wiki/Luis_A._Ferr%C3%A9" title="Luis A. Ferr\xc3\xa9">Luis A. Ferr\xc3\xa9</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Hern%C3%A1ndez_Col%C3%B3n" title="Rafael Hern\xc3\xa1ndez Col\xc3\xb3n">Rafael Hern\xc3\xa1ndez Col\xc3\xb3n</a>, both former <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Governor of Puerto Rico">governors of Puerto Rico</a>, as well as the childhood town of governor <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Sanchez_Vilella" class="mw-redirect" title="Roberto Sanchez Vilella">Roberto Sanchez Vilella</a>.\n</p><p>Statistics taken from the 2010 census show that 82.0% of Ponce\xc3\xb1os are <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">white</a> and 9.0% are <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">African-American</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno" title="Ta\xc3\xadno">Ta\xc3\xadnos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asians</a>, people of <a href="/wiki/Multiethnic" class="mw-redirect" title="Multiethnic">mixed race</a> and others making up the rest.<sup id="cite_ref-factfinder.census.gov_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factfinder.census.gov-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> At 82.0% vs. 76.2% for the island as a whole, Ponce has the highest concentration of white population of any municipality in Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, the US Census Bureau changed the definitions of its racial makeup categories for the 2020 Census<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> resulting in 19.0% of Ponce\xc3\xb1os being classified as <a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">white</a> and 13.3% as <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">Black/Afro Puerto Rican\'</a>, 0.3% as <a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asian</a>, and people of <a href="/wiki/Multiethnic" class="mw-redirect" title="Multiethnic">mixed race</a> making up the rest.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="1970s_economic_decline">1970s economic decline</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1970s economic decline"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The 1970s brought significant commercial, industrial and banking changes to Ponce that dramatically altered its financial stability and outlook of the city, the municipality and, to an extent, the entire southern Puerto Rico region. After <a href="/wiki/Luis_A._Ferre" class="mw-redirect" title="Luis A. Ferre">Luis A. Ferre</a> concluded his term as governor of Puerto Rico on January 1, 1973, he closed the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Iron_Works" title="Puerto Rico Iron Works">Puerto Rico Iron Works</a> foundry on <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_123" title="Puerto Rico Highway 123">Avenida Hostos</a>, and transferred the offices of Ponce\'s island-wide <a href="/wiki/El_Nuevo_Dia" class="mw-redirect" title="El Nuevo Dia">El Dia</a> newspaper that he owned, as well as the headquarters of his <a href="/w/index.php?title=Empresas_Ferr%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Empresas Ferr\xc3\xa9 (page does not exist)">Empresas Ferr\xc3\xa9</a>, to San Juan. In 1976, <a href="/wiki/CORCO" class="mw-redirect" title="CORCO">CORCO</a>\xe2\x80\x94southern Puerto Rico\'s main source of economic vitality\xe2\x80\x94shut down its industrial operations in <a href="/wiki/Guayanilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Guayanilla">Guayanilla</a> leaving thousands of area residents without work; its impact on indirect sources of employment was even greater. Also, the sugar cane industry, also suffered a major downturn. Sugar cane had until 1976 been grown and refined at Ponce\'s <a href="/wiki/Central_Mercedita" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Mercedita">Central Mercedita</a>, but in that year agricultural production of sugar cane was halted in the lands of the municipality of Ponce and adjacent towns. Also, the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Banco_de_Ponce" title="Banco de Ponce">Banco de Ponce</a> and <a href="/wiki/Banco_Cr%C3%A9dito_y_Ahorro_Ponce%C3%B1o" title="Banco Cr\xc3\xa9dito y Ahorro Ponce\xc3\xb1o">Banco Cr\xc3\xa9dito y Ahorro Ponce\xc3\xb1o</a> were moved to San Juan. Unemployment of Ponce jumped to 25% as a result of these changes.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="The_Mameyes_landslide">The Mameyes landslide</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: The Mameyes landslide"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mameyes.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Mameyes.jpg/220px-Mameyes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Mameyes.jpg/330px-Mameyes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Mameyes.jpg/440px-Mameyes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="539" /></a><figcaption>The 1985 <a href="/wiki/1985_Puerto_Rico_floods" title="1985 Puerto Rico floods">Mameyes landslide</a> in <a href="/wiki/Barrio_Portugu%C3%A9s_Urbano" class="mw-redirect" title="Barrio Portugu\xc3\xa9s Urbano">Barrio Portugu\xc3\xa9s Urbano</a> killed 129 people in the worst landslide disaster in North America to that date</figcaption></figure>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/1985_Puerto_Rico_floods" title="1985 Puerto Rico floods">1985 Puerto Rico floods</a></div>\n<p>On October 7, 1985, Ponce was the scene of a major tragedy, when at least 129 people lost their lives to a <a href="/wiki/Mudslide" class="mw-redirect" title="Mudslide">mudslide</a> in a sector of Barrio <a href="/wiki/Portugu%C3%A9s_Urbano" title="Portugu\xc3\xa9s Urbano">Portugu\xc3\xa9s Urbano</a><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> called <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Isabel_(1985)#Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical Storm Isabel (1985)">Mameyes</a>. International help was needed to rescue people and recover corpses. The United States and many other countries, including Mexico, France, and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, sent economic, human, and machinery relief. The commonwealth government, subsequently, relocated hundreds of people to a new community built on stable\nground.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2005, the National Science and Technology Council\'s Subcommittee on Disaster Reduction of the United States reported that the Mameyes landslide held the record for having inflicted "the greatest loss of life by a single landslide" up to that year.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Recent_history">Recent history</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Recent history"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">municipality</a> of Ponce became the first in Puerto Rico to obtain its <a href="/wiki/Autonomy" title="Autonomy">autonomy</a><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> on October 27, 1992, under a new law (<i>The Autonomous Municipalities Act of the Commonwealth of Puerto Rico</i><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>) enacted by the Puerto Rican legislature. <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of mayors of Ponce, Puerto Rico">Ponce\'s mayor</a> for 15 years, <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Cordero_Santiago" title="Rafael Cordero Santiago">Rafael Cordero Santiago</a> ("Churumba"), credited for leading the municipal government to that accomplishment, died in office on the morning of January 17, 2004, after suffering three consecutive strokes. Vice-mayor <a href="/wiki/Delis_Castillo_Rivera_de_Santiago" title="Delis Castillo Rivera de Santiago">Delis Castillo Rivera de Santiago</a> finished his term. Cordero was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Zayas_Seijo" title="Francisco Zayas Seijo">Francisco Zayas Seijo</a>. In the 2008 general elections <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Mel%C3%A9ndez" title="Mar\xc3\xada Mel\xc3\xa9ndez">Mar\xc3\xada "Mayita" Mel\xc3\xa9ndez</a> was elected mayor of the city of Ponce and served three terms.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The current (2021) mayor is <a href="/wiki/Luis_Irizarry_Pab%C3%B3n" title="Luis Irizarry Pab\xc3\xb3n">Luis Irizarry Pab\xc3\xb3n</a> who became the first mayoral candidate in the modern history of Ponce to win with more than 60% of votes cast.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The city is also the governmental seat of the Autonomous Municipality of Ponce, and the regional hub for various <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Government of Puerto Rico">commonwealth</a> entities. For example, it serves as the southern hub for the Judiciary of Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is also the regional center for various other commonwealth and <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">federal</a> government agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Ponce has improved its economy in the last years. In recent years, Ponce has solidified its position as the second most important city of Puerto Rico based on its economic progress and increasing population.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Today, the city of Ponce is the second largest in Puerto Rico outside of the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a> metropolitan area.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Its nicknames include: <i>La Perla del Sur</i> (The Pearl of the South)<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <i>La Ciudad Se\xc3\xb1orial</i> (The Noble or Lordly City).<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The city is also known as <i>La Ciudad de las Quenepas</i> (<a href="/wiki/Genip" class="mw-redirect" title="Genip">Genip</a> City),<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> from the abundant amount of this fruit that grows within its borders. The complete history of Ponce can be appreciated at the <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_la_Historia_de_Ponce" title="Museo de la Historia de Ponce">Museo de la Historia de Ponce</a>, which opened in the city in 1992. It depicts the history of the city from its early settlement days until the end of the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On September 20, 2017 <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> struck the island of Puerto Rico. In Ponce, $1,000 million in damages were the initial estimates. An estimated 3,500 homes were completely or partially destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The hurricane triggered numerous landslides in Ponce.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ponce_as_Viewed_from_the_Mountains.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Ponce_as_Viewed_from_the_Mountains.jpg/200px-Ponce_as_Viewed_from_the_Mountains.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="160" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Ponce_as_Viewed_from_the_Mountains.jpg/300px-Ponce_as_Viewed_from_the_Mountains.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Ponce_as_Viewed_from_the_Mountains.jpg/400px-Ponce_as_Viewed_from_the_Mountains.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2391" data-file-height="1913" /></a><figcaption>The municipality of Ponce includes many acres of lush forests like this one. The city of Ponce can be seen in the far background.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The Municipality of Ponce sits on the Southern Coastal Plain region of the Puerto Rico, on the shores of the Caribbean Sea. It is bordered by the municipalities of Adjuntas, Utuado, Jayuya, Pe\xc3\xb1uelas, and Juana D\xc3\xadaz.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\nPonce is a large municipality, with only <a href="/wiki/Arecibo" class="mw-redirect" title="Arecibo">Arecibo</a> larger in land area in Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In terms of physical features, the municipality occupies a roughly rectangular area in south-central portion of the Island of approximately 10 miles (16&#160;km) wide (east-to-west) by 13 miles (21&#160;km) long (north-to-south).<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It has a surface area of 116.0 square miles (300&#160;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The main physiographic features of the municipality of Ponce are: (1) the mountainous interior containing the headwaters of the main river systems, (2) an upper plain, (3) a range of predominantly east-west trending limestone hills, (4) a coastal plain, and (5) a coastal flat.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The northern two-thirds of the municipality consists of the mountainous interior, with the southern third divided between hills, coastal plains, and the coastal flat.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Ponce\'s municipal territory reaches the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">central mountain range</a> to the north and the Caribbean Sea to the south. Geographically speaking, the southern area of the territory is part of the Ponce-Patillas alluvial plain subsector and the southern coastal plain, which were created by the consolidation of the valleys of the southern side of the central mountain range and the Cayey mountain range. The central area of the municipality is part of the semi-arid southern hills. These two regions are classified as being the driest on the island. The northern part of the municipality is considered to be within the rainy western mountains.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Barrio <a href="/wiki/An%C3%B3n" title="An\xc3\xb3n">An\xc3\xb3n</a> is home to <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Maravilla" title="Cerro Maravilla">Cerro Maravilla</a>, a peak that at 4,085 feet (1,245&#160;m) is Puerto Rico\'s fourth highest peak.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Nineteen barrios<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> comprise the rural areas of the municipality, and the topology of their lands varies from flatlands to hills to steep mountain slopes. The hilly barrios of the municipality (moving clockwise around the outskirts of the city) are these seven: <a href="/wiki/Quebrada_Lim%C3%B3n" title="Quebrada Lim\xc3\xb3n">Quebrada Lim\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marue%C3%B1o" title="Marue\xc3\xb1o">Marue\xc3\xb1o</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magueyes" class="mw-redirect" title="Magueyes">Magueyes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tibes" title="Tibes">Tibes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugu%C3%A9s_Rural" class="mw-redirect" title="Portugu\xc3\xa9s Rural">Portugu\xc3\xa9s Rural</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machuelo_Arriba" title="Machuelo Arriba">Machuelo Arriba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cerrillos_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cerrillos (Ponce)">Cerrillos</a>. The barrios of <a href="/wiki/Canas_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Canas (Ponce)">Canas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coto_Laurel" title="Coto Laurel">Coto Laurel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capitanejo_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Capitanejo (Ponce)">Capitanejo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sabanetas_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sabanetas (Ponce)">Sabanetas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vayas" class="mw-redirect" title="Vayas">Vayas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bucan%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="Bucan\xc3\xa1">Bucan\xc3\xa1</a> also surround the outskirts of the city but these are mostly flat. The remaining six other barrios are further away from the city and their topology is rugged mountain terrain. These are (clockwise): <a href="/wiki/Guaraguao" title="Guaraguao">Guaraguao</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Patricio_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="San Patricio (Ponce)">San Patricio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monte_Llano" class="mw-redirect" title="Monte Llano">Monte Llano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marag%C3%BCez" title="Marag\xc3\xbcez">Marag\xc3\xbcez</a>, <a href="/wiki/An%C3%B3n" title="An\xc3\xb3n">An\xc3\xb3n</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Real_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Real (Ponce)">Real</a>. The ruggedness of these barrios is because through these areas of the municipality runs the <a href="/wiki/Cordillera_Central_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Cordillera Central (Puerto Rico)">Central Mountain Range</a> of the Island.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The remaining barrios are part of the urban zone of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There are six barrios in the core urban zone of the municipality named <i><a href="/wiki/Primero_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Primero (Ponce)">Primero</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Segundo_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Segundo (Ponce)">Segundo</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Tercero" class="mw-redirect" title="Tercero">Tercero</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Cuarto_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuarto (Ponce)">Cuarto</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Quinto_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Quinto (Ponce)">Quinto</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Sexto" class="mw-redirect" title="Sexto">Sexto</a>.</i> They are delimetered by streets, rivers, or major highways. For example, Barrio Tercero is bounded in the north by Isabel Street, in the east by the Rio Portugu\xc3\xa9s, in the south by Comercio Street, and the west by <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Las_Delicias" title="Plaza Las Delicias">Plaza Las Delicias</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Barrio Tercero includes much of what is called the historic district.\n</p><p>There is a seismic detector that the University of Puerto Rico, Mayag\xc3\xbcez Campus, has placed in Barrio Cerrillos.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Land_features">Land features</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Land features"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Cruzeta_El_Vigia.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cruzeta_El_Vigia.JPG/200px-Cruzeta_El_Vigia.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cruzeta_El_Vigia.JPG/300px-Cruzeta_El_Vigia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Cruzeta_El_Vigia.JPG/400px-Cruzeta_El_Vigia.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1728" data-file-height="2304" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Cruceta_del_Vig%C3%ADa" title="Cruceta del Vig\xc3\xada">Cruceta del Vig\xc3\xada</a> marks the spot where during the 17th through 19th centuries a guard watched for merchant as well as enemy ships approaching the Ponce harbor 3&#160;mi (5&#160;km) away.</figcaption></figure>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mountains_in_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of mountains in Ponce, Puerto Rico">List of mountains in Ponce, Puerto Rico</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of islands of Ponce, Puerto Rico">List of islands of Ponce, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>Elevations include <a href="/wiki/Cerro_de_Punta" title="Cerro de Punta">Cerro de Punta</a> at 4,390 feet (1,340&#160;m), the highest in Puerto Rico, located in Barrio <a href="/wiki/An%C3%B3n" title="An\xc3\xb3n">An\xc3\xb3n</a> in the territory of the municipality of Ponce.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Mount Jayuya, at 4,314 feet (1,315&#160;m) is located on the boundary between Barrio An\xc3\xb3n and Barrio Saliente in Jayuya. <a href="/wiki/Cerro_Maravilla" title="Cerro Maravilla">Cerro Maravilla</a>, at nearly 3,970 feet (1,210&#160;m) above sea level, is located to the east of Barrio An\xc3\xb3n. There are many other mountains at lower elevations in the municipality, such as the Montes Llanos ridge and Mount Diablo, at 2,231 feet (680&#160;m) and Mount Marue\xc3\xb1o, at 2,100 feet (640&#160;m), and Pinto Peak, among others. Part of the <a href="/wiki/Toro_Negro_State_Forest" title="Toro Negro State Forest">Toro Negro Forest</a> is located in Barrio An\xc3\xb3n. Coastal <a href="/wiki/Promontory" title="Promontory">promontories</a> include Cuchara, Pe\xc3\xb1oncillo, Carnero, and Cabull\xc3\xb3n points.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Fifty-six percent of the municipality consists of slopes 10 degrees or greater.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Water_features">Water features</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Water features"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Ponce" class="mw-redirect" title="List of rivers of Ponce">List of rivers of Ponce</a></div>\n<p>The 14 rivers comprising the hydrographic system of Ponce are <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Matilde" title="R\xc3\xado Matilde">Matilde</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Inab%C3%B3n" title="R\xc3\xado Inab\xc3\xb3n">Inab\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Bucan%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Bucan\xc3\xa1">Bucan\xc3\xa1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacaguas_River" title="Jacaguas River">Jacaguas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_Portugu%C3%A9s" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio Portugu\xc3\xa9s">Portugu\xc3\xa9s</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Ca%C3%B1as_(Ponce,_Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Ca\xc3\xb1as (Ponce, Puerto Rico)">Ca\xc3\xb1as</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Pastillo" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Pastillo">Pastillo</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Cerrillos" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Cerrillos">Cerrillos</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Chiquito_(Ponce,_Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Chiquito (Ponce, Puerto Rico)">Chiquito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rio_Bayagan" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio Bayagan">Bayagan</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Blanco_(Ponce,_Puerto_Rico)" title="R\xc3\xado Blanco (Ponce, Puerto Rico)">Blanco</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Prieto_(Ponce,_Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Prieto (Ponce, Puerto Rico)">Prieto</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_An%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado An\xc3\xb3n">An\xc3\xb3n</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_San_Patricio" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado San Patricio">San Patricio</a><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Jacaguas River runs for a brief stretch on the southeast area of the municipality. The Inab\xc3\xb3n River springs from An\xc3\xb3n ward and runs through the municipality for some 18&#160;mi (29.0&#160;km); the tributaries of the Inab\xc3\xb3n are the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_An%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado An\xc3\xb3n">An\xc3\xb3n</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Guayo" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Guayo">Guayo</a> rivers and the Emajagua Brook. The Bucan\xc3\xa1 River springs from Machuelo Arriba ward and runs for 18.5&#160;mi (29.8&#160;km) into the Caribbean Sea. The tributaries of the Bucan\xc3\xa1 are the San Patricio, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Bayag%C3%A1n" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Bayag\xc3\xa1n">Bayag\xc3\xa1n</a>, and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Prieto_(Ponce,_Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Prieto (Ponce, Puerto Rico)">Prieto</a> Rivers and Ausubo brook. The Portugu\xc3\xa9s River springs from the ward of that name in Adjuntas, and runs for 17.3&#160;mi (27.8&#160;km) into the Caribbean sea at Ponce Playa ward. The Matilde River, also known as the Pastillo River, runs for 12&#160;mi (19&#160;km); its tributaries are the Ca\xc3\xb1as River and the Lim\xc3\xb3n and del Agua brooks. Lakes in Ponce include Bronce and Ponce\xc3\xb1a as well as lakes bearing numbers: Uno, Dos, Tres, and Cinco; and the Salinas Lagoon, which is considered a restricted lagoon.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other water bodies are the springs at Quintana and the <a href="/wiki/Paseo_Tablado_La_Guancha" title="Paseo Tablado La Guancha">La Guancha</a> and <a href="/wiki/El_Tuque" title="El Tuque">El Tuque</a> beaches.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There is also a beach at <a href="/wiki/Isla_de_Caja_de_Muertos,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Isla de Caja de Muertos, Puerto Rico">Caja de Muertos Island</a>. <a href="/wiki/Lake_Cerrillos" title="Lake Cerrillos">Lake Cerrillos</a> is located within the limits of the municipality,<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> as will be the future lake resulting from the <a href="/wiki/Portugu%C3%A9s_Dam" title="Portugu\xc3\xa9s Dam">Portugu\xc3\xa9s Dam</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cerrillos_State_Forest" title="Cerrillos State Forest">Cerrillos State Forest</a> is also located in the municipality of Ponce.\n</p><p>Coastal geographic features in Ponce include <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%ADa_de_Ponce" title="Bah\xc3\xada de Ponce">Bah\xc3\xada de Ponce</a>, Caleta de Cabullones (Cabullones Cove), and five cays: <a href="/wiki/Isla_de_Jueyes" title="Isla de Jueyes">Jueyes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isla_de_Ratones_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Isla de Ratones (Ponce)">Ratones</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Isla_Cardona" title="Isla Cardona">Cardona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gatas_(Ponce)" title="Gatas (Ponce)">Gatas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Isla_del_Frio" class="mw-redirect" title="Isla del Frio">Isla del Frio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Isla_de_Caja_de_Muertos,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Isla de Caja de Muertos, Puerto Rico">Caja de Muertos Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Morrillito" title="Morrillito">Morrillito</a> islet are located at the boundary between Ponce and Juana D\xc3\xadaz. There is a <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">mangrove</a> covering an area of approximately 100 acres (40&#160;ha) at Cabull\xc3\xb3n promontory and Isla del Frio. The Salinas Lagoon, part of <a href="/wiki/Reserva_Natural_Punta_Cucharas" title="Reserva Natural Punta Cucharas">Reserva Natural Punta Cucharas</a>, has a mangrove that expands about 37 acres (15&#160;ha). The lagoon itself consists of 698 <i>cuerdas</i> (678&#160;acres; 274&#160;ha).<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Rita cave is located in Barrio Cerrillos.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Climate">Climate</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Climate"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Ponce features a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">tropical savanna climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">Koppen Aw/As</a>). Ponce has summer highs averaging 92&#160;\xc2\xb0F (33&#160;\xc2\xb0C)<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and winter highs, 87&#160;\xc2\xb0F (31&#160;\xc2\xb0C).<sup id="cite_ref-weather.com_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather.com-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It has lows averaging 67&#160;\xc2\xb0F (19&#160;\xc2\xb0C) in the winter<sup id="cite_ref-weather.com_150-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather.com-150"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and 74&#160;\xc2\xb0F (23&#160;\xc2\xb0C) in the summer.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It has a record high of 100&#160;\xc2\xb0F (38&#160;\xc2\xb0C), which occurred on 21 August 2003,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and a record low of 51&#160;\xc2\xb0F (11&#160;\xc2\xb0C) which occurred on 28 February 2004, tying the record low of 51&#160;\xc2\xb0F (11&#160;\xc2\xb0C) from 25 January 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The mean annual temperature in the municipality is 79&#160;\xc2\xb0F (26&#160;\xc2\xb0C).<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible" style="width:auto; text-align:center; line-height:1.2em;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="14">Climate
