Ponce\'s tourist attractions <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zD5nkoR8t3Y"><b>HERE</b></a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Ponce_en_Marcha"><i>Ponce en Marcha</i></h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ponce en Marcha"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-center" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ciudad_de_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico,_vista_desde_el_Hotel_Ponce_Holiday_Inn,_mirando_al_este_(DSC02782D).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Ciudad_de_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_vista_desde_el_Hotel_Ponce_Holiday_Inn%2C_mirando_al_este_%28DSC02782D%29.jpg/900px-Ciudad_de_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_vista_desde_el_Hotel_Ponce_Holiday_Inn%2C_mirando_al_este_%28DSC02782D%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="900" height="261" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Ciudad_de_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_vista_desde_el_Hotel_Ponce_Holiday_Inn%2C_mirando_al_este_%28DSC02782D%29.jpg/1350px-Ciudad_de_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_vista_desde_el_Hotel_Ponce_Holiday_Inn%2C_mirando_al_este_%28DSC02782D%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Ciudad_de_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_vista_desde_el_Hotel_Ponce_Holiday_Inn%2C_mirando_al_este_%28DSC02782D%29.jpg/1800px-Ciudad_de_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_vista_desde_el_Hotel_Ponce_Holiday_Inn%2C_mirando_al_este_%28DSC02782D%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3243" data-file-height="939" /></a><figcaption>Skyline of the city of Ponce in 2020, looking east. The city\'s tallest tower, the 23-story <i>Condominio El Mirador</i>, is next to the extreme right, with the two towers of <a href="/wiki/Hospital_Damas" title="Hospital Damas">Hospital Damas</a> to its right.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In recent years an intensive $440 million<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>176<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>177<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> revitalization project called "<i>Ponce en Marcha</i>"<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>178<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> ("Ponce on the Move") has increased the city\'s historic area from 260 to 1,046 buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>179<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <i>Ponce en Marcha</i><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>d<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> project was conceived in 1985 by then governor <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Hern%C3%A1ndez_Col%C3%B3n" title="Rafael Hern\xc3\xa1ndez Col\xc3\xb3n">Rafael Hern\xc3\xa1ndez Col\xc3\xb3n</a> during his second term in <a href="/wiki/La_Fortaleza" title="La Fortaleza">La Fortaleza</a> and Ponce mayor <a href="/wiki/Jose_Dapena_Thompson" class="mw-redirect" title="Jose Dapena Thompson">Jose Dapena Thompson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>180<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>181<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The plan was approved by the Ponce Municipal Legislature on January 14, 2003. It was signed by Governor Sila Calderon via <a href="/wiki/Executive_order_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive order (United States)">Executive Order</a> on December 28, 2003, and went into effect on January 12, 2004. The plan incorporates one billion dollars in spending during the period of 2004 through 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>182<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A significant number of buildings in Ponce are listed in the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places_listings_in_southern_Puerto_Rico" title="National Register of Historic Places listings in southern Puerto Rico">National Register of Historic Places</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>183<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The nonprofit <i>Project for Public Places</i><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>184<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> listed the <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Historic_Zone" title="Ponce Historic Zone">historic downtown Ponce city center</a> as one of the <i>60 of the World\'s Great Places</i>, for its "graciously preserved showcase of Caribbean culture".<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>185<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The revitalized historic area of the city goes by various names, including "Ponce Centro" (Ponce Center),<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>186<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> "Historic Ponce",<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>187<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and "Historic District."<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>188<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The name "Ponce en Marcha" comes from the revitalization plan of <i>Zona Atocha</i> in Madrid called <i>Atocha en Marcha</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>189<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Landmarks">Landmarks</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Landmarks"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Fuente_de_los_Leones_-_Ponce_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Fuente_de_los_Leones_-_Ponce_Puerto_Rico.jpg/250px-Fuente_de_los_Leones_-_Ponce_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Fuente_de_los_Leones_-_Ponce_Puerto_Rico.jpg/375px-Fuente_de_los_Leones_-_Ponce_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Fuente_de_los_Leones_-_Ponce_Puerto_Rico.jpg/500px-Fuente_de_los_Leones_-_Ponce_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a><figcaption>The Lions Fountain in <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Las_Delicias" title="Plaza Las Delicias">Plaza Las Delicias</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>The city has been christened as <i>Museum City</i> for its many quality museums.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>190<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>191<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> All museums in Ponce are under municipal government administration. On 15 September 2004, the last four museums not under local control were transferred from the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Puerto_Rican_Culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Institute of Puerto Rican Culture">Institute of Puerto Rican Culture</a> to the Ponce Municipal Government by act of the Puerto Rico Legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>192<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, these four museums (<a href="/wiki/Armstrong-Poventud_Residence" class="mw-redirect" title="Armstrong-Poventud Residence">Casa Armstrong Poventud</a>, <a href="/wiki/Casa_Wiechers-Villaronga" title="Casa Wiechers-Villaronga">Casa Wiechers-Villaronga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_la_M%C3%BAsica_Puertorrique%C3%B1a" title="Museo de la M\xc3\xbasica Puertorrique\xc3\xb1a">Museo de la M\xc3\xbasica Puertorrique\xc3\xb1a</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_la_Masacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Casa de la Masacre">Casa de la Masacre</a>) continue to be controlled by the ICP.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>193<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>194<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Downtown Ponce in particular features several museums and landmarks.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>195<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Plaza_Las_Delicias" title="Plaza Las Delicias">Plaza Las Delicias</a>, the town\'s main square, features a prominent fountain (namely, the "Lions Fountain"), the <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="Ponce Cathedral">Ponce Cathedral</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Parque_de_Bombas" title="Parque de Bombas">Parque de Bombas</a>, an old fire house, now a museum, that stands as an iconic symbol of the city and a tribute to the bravery of its firefighters. This plaza is also a usual gathering place for "ponce\xc3\xb1os". Other buildings around Ponce\'s main plaza include the Casa Alcald\xc3\xada (<a href="/wiki/Ponce_City_Hall" title="Ponce City Hall">Ponce City Hall</a>), the oldest colonial building in the city, dating to the 1840s, and the <a href="/wiki/Armstrong-Poventud_Residence" class="mw-redirect" title="Armstrong-Poventud Residence">Armstrong-Poventud Residence</a>, an example of the <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">neoclassical</a> architectural heritage of the island.\n</p><p>Just north of downtown Ponce lies the <a href="/wiki/Castillo_Serrall%C3%A9s" title="Castillo Serrall\xc3\xa9s">Castillo Serrall\xc3\xa9s</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cruceta_del_Vig%C3%ADa" title="Cruceta del Vig\xc3\xada">Cruceta del Vig\xc3\xada</a>, a 100-foot (30&#160;m) observation tower which overlooks the city. The Serralles castle is reported to receive nearly 100,000 visitors every year.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>196<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The hill on which the Cruceta is located was originally used by scouts to scan for incoming mercantile ships as well as invading ones. The invasion of American troops in 1898 was first spotted from there.\n</p><p>Ponce is home to Puerto Rico\'s oldest cemetery; in fact, it is the oldest cemetery in the <a href="/wiki/Antilles" title="Antilles">Antilles</a>. In the city outskirts, the <a href="/wiki/Tibes_Indigenous_Ceremonial_Center" title="Tibes Indigenous Ceremonial Center">Tibes Indigenous Ceremonial Center</a> was discovered in 1975 after hurricane rains uncovered <a href="/wiki/Pottery" title="Pottery">pottery</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>197<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The center is the site of the oldest cemetery uncovered up to date in the Antilles. With some 200 skeletons unearthed from the year 300 AD, it is considered the largest and the most important archaeological finding in the West Indies.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>198<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>199<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Two other cemeteries in Ponce worth noting are the <a href="/wiki/Pante%C3%B3n_Nacional_Rom%C3%A1n_Baldorioty_de_Castro" title="Pante\xc3\xb3n Nacional Rom\xc3\xa1n Baldorioty de Castro">Pante\xc3\xb3n Nacional Rom\xc3\xa1n Baldorioty de Castro</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cementerio_Catolico_San_Vicente_de_Paul" class="mw-redirect" title="Cementerio Catolico San Vicente de Paul">Cementerio Catolico San Vicente de Paul</a>, both of which are listed in the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places_listings_in_southern_Puerto_Rico" title="National Register of Historic Places listings in southern Puerto Rico">National Register of Historic Places</a>. The Cementerio Catolico San Vicente de Paul has the most eye-catching burial constructions of any cemetery for the wealthiest families, both local and foreign-born, of southern Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>200<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Guancha.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/La_Guancha.jpg/250px-La_Guancha.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/La_Guancha.jpg/375px-La_Guancha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/La_Guancha.jpg/500px-La_Guancha.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/La_Guancha_Boardwalk" class="mw-redirect" title="La Guancha Boardwalk">La Guancha Boardwalk</a> as seen from the Boardwalk\'s observation tower</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Also in the city outskirts is <a href="/wiki/Hacienda_Buena_Vista" title="Hacienda Buena Vista">Hacienda Buena Vista</a>, an estate built in 1833 originally to grow fruits. It was converted into a <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">plantation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gristmill" title="Gristmill">gristmill</a> in 1845. It remained in operation until 1937, then fell into disrepair, but was restored by the government\'s <i>Fideicomiso de Conservaci\xc3\xb3n de Puerto Rico</i>. All the machinery works (the metal parts) are original, operated by water channeled from the 360m Vives waterfall; there is a hydraulic <a href="/wiki/Turbine" title="Turbine">turbine</a> which makes the corn mill work.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Paseo_Tablado_La_Guancha" title="Paseo Tablado La Guancha">Paseo Tablado La Guancha</a> is located in the town\'s sea shore. It features kiosks with food and beverages, an open-space stage for activities, and a <a href="/wiki/Marina" title="Marina">marina</a> called <a href="/wiki/Club_N%C3%A1utico_de_Ponce" title="Club N\xc3\xa1utico de Ponce">Club N\xc3\xa1utico de Ponce</a>. From the observation tower on the boardwalk, <a href="/wiki/Cardona_Island_Light" title="Cardona Island Light">Cardona Island Light</a> can be seen. A 45-minute boat ride is also available to <a href="/wiki/Isla_de_Caja_de_Muertos,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Isla de Caja de Muertos, Puerto Rico">Isla de Caja de Muertos</a> (Coffin Island), a small island with several beaches and an 1887 <a href="/wiki/Caja_de_Muertos_Light" title="Caja de Muertos Light">lighthouse</a>.\n</p><p>As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the city had also engaged in the development of a convention center with a capacity for 3,000 people. It is also to include two major hotels, apartment buildings and recreational facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>201<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Puerto Rico Route 143 (<a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_143" title="Puerto Rico Highway 143">PR-143</a>), known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Ruta_Panor%C3%A1mica" title="Ruta Panor\xc3\xa1mica">Panoramic Route</a></i>, runs edging near the municipality\'s northern border.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>202<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;" class=""></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of museums in Ponce, Puerto Rico">List of museums in Ponce, Puerto Rico</a>; <a href="/wiki/List_of_libraries_in_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of libraries in Ponce, Puerto Rico">List of libraries in Ponce, Puerto Rico</a>; and <a href="/wiki/List_of_events_in_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of events in Ponce, Puerto Rico">List of events in Ponce, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>The city is home to a long <a href="/wiki/List_of_Puerto_Rico_landmarks#Ponce" title="List of Puerto Rico landmarks">list of cultural assets</a> including libraries, museums, galleries, and parks, hundreds of buildings of historical value including schools, residences, bridges, and estates, and frequent activities such as festivals and carnivals. The municipality invests close to half a million dollars in promoting its cultural assets.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>203<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It established its first <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Municipal_Library" title="Ponce Municipal Library">library</a> in 1894<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>204<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and, as of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> had a <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Municipal_Library" title="Ponce Municipal Library">new central library</a><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>205<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> with seven other branches scattered throughout the municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>206<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:CasaPaoli_JuanLlanesSantosPRSHPO_pic2_MainFacade.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/CasaPaoli_JuanLlanesSantosPRSHPO_pic2_MainFacade.jpg/200px-CasaPaoli_JuanLlanesSantosPRSHPO_pic2_MainFacade.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/CasaPaoli_JuanLlanesSantosPRSHPO_pic2_MainFacade.jpg/300px-CasaPaoli_JuanLlanesSantosPRSHPO_pic2_MainFacade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/CasaPaoli_JuanLlanesSantosPRSHPO_pic2_MainFacade.jpg/400px-CasaPaoli_JuanLlanesSantosPRSHPO_pic2_MainFacade.jpg 2x" data-file-width="727" data-file-height="601" /></a><figcaption>The childhood home in Ponce of <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Paoli" title="Antonio Paoli">Antonio Paoli</a>, one of Puerto Rico\'s greatest musical performers</figcaption></figure>\n<p>A number of cultural events take place during the year, most prominently:<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>207<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>208<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>February \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Carnival" class="mw-redirect" title="Ponce Carnival">Ponce Carnival</a></li>\n<li>March \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Feria_de_Artesan%C3%ADas_de_Ponce" title="Feria de Artesan\xc3\xadas de Ponce">Feria de Artesan\xc3\xadas de Ponce</a> (Ponce Crafts Fair)<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>209<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2019, the 45th <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Feria de Artesan\xc3\xadas de Ponce</i></span> was held.<sup id="cite_ref-Primera_Hora_2019_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Primera_Hora_2019-216"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>210<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>April \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Jazz_Festival" title="Ponce Jazz Festival">Ponce Jazz Festival</a></li>\n<li>May \xe2\x80\x93\xe2\x80\x94 <a href="/wiki/Fiesta_Nacional_de_la_Danza" title="Fiesta Nacional de la Danza">Fiesta Nacional de la Danza</a>; Barrio <a href="/wiki/Playa_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Playa (Ponce)">Playa</a> Festival</li>\n<li>July \xe2\x80\x93 Barrio <a href="/wiki/San_Anton" class="mw-redirect" title="San Anton">San Anton</a>\'s Bomba Festival</li>\n<li>August \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Festival_Nacional_de_la_Quenepa" title="Festival Nacional de la Quenepa">Festival Nacional de la Quenepa</a> (National Genip Festival), often the third week<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>211<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>212<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>September \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/D%C3%ADa_Mundial_de_Ponce" title="D\xc3\xada Mundial de Ponce">D\xc3\xada Mundial de Ponce</a></li>\n<li>November \xe2\x80\x93 Discovering Our Indian Roots</li>\n<li>December \xe2\x80\x93 Patron Saint\'s Day Festival (<i><a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">Fiestas Patronales</a></i>);<sup id="cite_ref-periodicolaperla.com_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-periodicolaperla.com-219"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>213<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Las_Ma%C3%B1anitas" title="Las Ma\xc3\xb1anitas">Las Ma\xc3\xb1anitas</a></i>;<sup id="cite_ref-periodicolaperla.com_219-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-periodicolaperla.com-219"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>213<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Coro_de_Ni%C3%B1os_de_Ponce" title="Coro de Ni\xc3\xb1os de Ponce">Children\'s Christmas Concert</a></li></ul>\n<p>The city values its cultural traditions as evidenced by the revitalization project <i>Ponce en Marcha.</i> It is deeply rooted in its traditional cultural, artistic, and musical heritage. The love for art and architecture, for example, can be appreciated at its museums of art, music, and architecture.\n</p>\n<blockquote><p>"Over the last century or so, the north [i.e., San Juan] willingly accepted the influence of <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">western culture</a> with its tendency toward large sprawling metropolises, and the displacement of old values and attitudes. Ponce, on the other hand, has been content to retain its old <a href="/wiki/Traditions" class="mw-redirect" title="Traditions">traditions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Culture" title="Culture">culture</a>. Ponce is not concerned about losing its long standing position as the second largest city in population after San Juan. On the contrary, she prefers to maintain her current size, and stick to its old traditions and culture."<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>214<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>215<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>Some argue that the Ponce\xc3\xb1o culture is different from the rest of the Island: \n</p>\n<blockquote><p>"Ponce\xc3\xb1os have always been a breed apart from other Puerto Ricans. Their insularity and haughtiness are legendary, and some Puerto Ricans claim that even the dialect in Ponce is slightly different from that spoken in the rest of the Island. They are also racially different: you\'ll see more people of African descent in Ponce than anywhere else in the Island except <a href="/wiki/Loiza,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Loiza, Puerto Rico">Loiza</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>216<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></p></blockquote><p>Others claim that Ponce\xc3\xb1os exhibit considerable more civic pride than do residents of other locales.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>217<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Rivera" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Rivera">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Rivera</a>, the most important statesman in the Island at the close of the 19th century, referred to Ponce as "the most Puerto Rican city of Puerto Rico."<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>218<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>e<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Music">Music</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Music"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Artists_in_the_Making.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Artists_in_the_Making.jpg/200px-Artists_in_the_Making.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="160" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Artists_in_the_Making.jpg/300px-Artists_in_the_Making.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Artists_in_the_Making.jpg/400px-Artists_in_the_Making.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2184" data-file-height="1747" /></a><figcaption>Children performing at the annual <a href="/wiki/Feria_de_Artesan%C3%ADas_de_Ponce" title="Feria de Artesan\xc3\xadas de Ponce">Feria de Artesan\xc3\xadas de Ponce</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ponce_City_Hall" title="Ponce City Hall">Ponce City Hall</a> is visible in the background.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Artistic development also flourished during this period. The surging of popular rhythms like <a href="/wiki/Bomba_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Bomba (Puerto Rico)">Bomba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plena" title="Plena">Plena</a> took place in the south region of the island, mainly in Ponce. Barrio San Ant\xc3\xb3n is known as one of the birthplaces of the rhythm. Every July, Ponce celebrates an annual festival of Bomba and Plena, which includes various musicians and parades.\n</p><p>Immigrants from Spain, Italy, France, Germany, and England came to Ponce to develop an international city that still maintains rich <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> and African heritage. The African personality, belief, and music add flavor and colorful rhythm to Ponce\'s culture. Part of this are the influences of the <a href="/wiki/Bomba_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Bomba (Puerto Rico)">Bomba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plena" title="Plena">Plena</a> rhythms. These are a combination and Caribbean and African music.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>219<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Ponce has also been the birthplace of several singers and musicians. From <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a> singers like <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Paoli" title="Antonio Paoli">Antonio Paoli</a>, who lived in the early 20th century, to contemporary singers like <a href="/wiki/Ednita_Nazario" title="Ednita Nazario">Ednita Nazario</a>. Also, <a href="/wiki/Salsa_music" title="Salsa music">Salsa</a> singers like <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9ctor_Lavoe" title="H\xc3\xa9ctor Lavoe">H\xc3\xa9ctor Lavoe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheo_Feliciano" title="Cheo Feliciano">Cheo Feliciano</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ismael_Quintana" title="Ismael Quintana">Ismael Quintana</a> also come from the city.\n</p><p>Dating back to 1858, <a href="/wiki/Carnaval_de_Ponce" title="Carnaval de Ponce">Ponce\'s Carnival</a> is the oldest in Puerto Rico, and acquired an international flavor for its 150th anniversary.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>220<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is one of the oldest <a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">carnivals</a> celebrated in the Western Hemisphere. It features various parades with masked characters representative of good and evil.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Puerto_Rican_Music" class="mw-redirect" title="Museum of Puerto Rican Music">Museum of Puerto Rican Music</a>, located at the Serrall\xc3\xa9s-Nev\xc3\xa1rez family residence in downtown Ponce, illustrates music history on the Island, most of which had its origin and development in Ponce.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>221<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>No discussion of music in Ponce would be complete without rendering honor to the great performances of King of Tenors <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Paoli" title="Antonio Paoli">Antonio Paoli</a> and danza master <a href="/wiki/Juan_Morel_Campos" title="Juan Morel Campos">Juan Morel Campos</a>, both from Ponce. Today, there is a statue of Juan Morel Campos that adorns the Plaza Las Delicias city square, and the <a href="/wiki/Casa_Paoli" title="Casa Paoli">home</a> where Paoli was born and raised functions as the Puerto Rico Center for Folkloric Research, a research center for Puerto Rican culture.\n</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Municipal_Band" title="Ponce Municipal Band">municipal band</a> presents concerts every Sunday evening, and a Youth Symphony Orchestra also performs.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>222<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Arts">Arts</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Arts"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Museo_de_Arte,_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico-Exterior.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Museo_de_Arte%2C_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico-Exterior.jpg/200px-Museo_de_Arte%2C_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico-Exterior.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Museo_de_Arte%2C_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico-Exterior.jpg/300px-Museo_de_Arte%2C_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico-Exterior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Museo_de_Arte%2C_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico-Exterior.jpg/400px-Museo_de_Arte%2C_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico-Exterior.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_Arte_de_Ponce" title="Museo de Arte de Ponce">Museo de Arte de Ponce</a>, the largest art museum in the Caribbean,<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>223<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is a mecca for the arts in the Island</figcaption></figure>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_theaters_in_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of theaters in Ponce, Puerto Rico">List of theaters in Ponce, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>Ponce\'s love for the arts dates back to at least 1864 when the <a href="/wiki/Teatro_La_Perla" title="Teatro La Perla">Teatro La Perla</a> was built. Ponce is also the birthplace of artists like <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Pou" title="Miguel Pou">Miguel Pou</a>, Horacio Castaing, and several others in the fields of <a href="/wiki/Painting" title="Painting">painting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sculpture" title="Sculpture">sculpture</a>, and others. The City is one of only seven cities in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">Western Hemisphere</a> (the others being <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valpara%C3%ADso" title="Valpara\xc3\xadso">Valpara\xc3\xadso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mar_del_Plata" title="Mar del Plata">Mar del Plata</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rosario" title="Rosario">Rosario</a>) in the Ruta Europea del Modernisme,<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>224<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> an international <a href="/wiki/Non-profit" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-profit">non-profit</a> association for the promotion and protection of <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a> heritage in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>225<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Today, Ponce has more museums (nine) than any other municipality in the Island.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>226<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ponce is home to the <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_Arte_de_Ponce" title="Museo de Arte de Ponce">Museo de Arte de Ponce</a> (MAP), founded in 1959 by fellow <i>ponce\xc3\xb1o</i> <a href="/wiki/Luis_A._Ferr%C3%A9" title="Luis A. Ferr\xc3\xa9">Luis A. Ferr\xc3\xa9</a>. The museum was operated by Ferr\xc3\xa9 until his death at the age of 99, and it is now under the direction of the Luis A. Ferr\xc3\xa9 Foundation. Designed by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Durell_Stone" title="Edward Durell Stone">Edward Durell Stone</a>, architect of <a href="/wiki/Radio_City_Music_Hall" title="Radio City Music Hall">Radio City Music Hall</a><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>227<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Modern_Art" title="Museum of Modern Art">Museum of Modern Art</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>, MAP is the only museum of international stature on the Island, the only one that was accredited by the <a href="/wiki/American_Alliance_of_Museums" title="American Alliance of Museums">American Alliance of Museums</a> (AAM),<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>228<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the only one that has received a design prize of honor from the <a href="/wiki/American_Institute_of_Architects" title="American Institute of Architects">American Institute of Architects</a> (AIA).<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>229<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It houses the most extensive art collection in the Caribbean with 4,500 pieces.<sup id="cite_ref-Discover_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Discover-237"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>230<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Auditorio_Juan_Pach%C3%ADn_Vic%C3%A9ns,_Bo._Canas_Urbano,_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico,_mirando_al_oeste.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Auditorio_Juan_Pach%C3%ADn_Vic%C3%A9ns%2C_Bo._Canas_Urbano%2C_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_mirando_al_oeste.jpg/200px-Auditorio_Juan_Pach%C3%ADn_Vic%C3%A9ns%2C_Bo._Canas_Urbano%2C_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_mirando_al_oeste.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3a/Auditorio_Juan_Pach%C3%ADn_Vic%C3%A9ns%2C_Bo._Canas_Urbano%2C_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico%2C_mirando_al_oeste.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="225" /></a><figcaption>Juan Pach\xc3\xadn Vic\xc3\xa9ns Auditorium, home to various sporting events in Ponce</figcaption></figure>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Grand_Prix" class="mw-redirect" title="Ponce Grand Prix">Ponce Grand Prix</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cruce_a_Nado_Internacional" title="Cruce a Nado Internacional">Cruce a Nado Internacional</a></div>\n<p>Most of Ponce\'s professional teams are called the <i>Leones de Ponce</i> (<i>Ponce Lions</i>, or <i><a href="/wiki/Leonas_de_Ponce" title="Leonas de Ponce">Ponce Lionesses</a></i> as the case may be) regardless of the sport. The <a href="/wiki/Leones_de_Ponce_(basketball)" title="Leones de Ponce (basketball)">Leones de Ponce</a> basketball team is one of the leading teams of the island, winning 12 championships during their tenure.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>231<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The team\'s venue is the <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pach%C3%ADn_Vic%C3%A9ns_Auditorium" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan Pach\xc3\xadn Vic\xc3\xa9ns Auditorium">Juan Pach\xc3\xadn Vic\xc3\xa9ns Auditorium</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Leones_de_Ponce_(baseball)" title="Leones de Ponce (baseball)">Leones de Ponce</a> (men\'s) baseball and the <a href="/wiki/Leonas_de_Ponce" title="Leonas de Ponce">Leonas de Ponce</a> (women\'s) baseball teams have also been fairly successful.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>232<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The baseball teams\' venue is the <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Montaner_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Francisco Montaner Stadium">Francisco Montaner Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>233<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The stadium is located next to the Juan Pach\xc3\xadn Vic\xc3\xa9ns Auditorium.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>234<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1993 the city hosted the <a href="/wiki/1993_Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="1993 Central American and Caribbean Games">Central American and Caribbean Games</a>, from November 19\xe2\x80\x9330.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>235<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The city also hosts two international annual sporting events. In the month of May, it hosts the <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Grand_Prix" class="mw-redirect" title="Ponce Grand Prix">Ponce Grand Prix</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a> event in which over 100 athletes participate. During the <a href="/wiki/Memorial_Day_Weekend" class="mw-redirect" title="Memorial Day Weekend">Memorial Day Weekend</a> in the month of September, the city hosts <a href="/wiki/Cruce_a_Nado_Internacional" title="Cruce a Nado Internacional">Cruce a Nado Internacional</a>, a swimming competition with over a dozen countries represented. Also, the <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Marathon" title="Ponce Marathon">Ponce Marathon</a> takes place every December, sometimes as part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Las_Ma%C3%B1anitas#Puerto_Rico" title="Las Ma\xc3\xb1anitas">Las Ma\xc3\xb1anitas</a></i> event on December 12.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Museo_Francisco_Pancho_Coimbre" class="mw-redirect" title="Museo Francisco Pancho Coimbre">Francisco "Pancho" Coimbre Sports Museum</a>, named after the <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Coimbre" class="mw-redirect" title="Francisco Coimbre">baseball player</a> of the same name, was dedicated to the honor of Puerto Rico\'s great sports men and women.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>236<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is located on the grounds of the <a href="/wiki/Charles_H._Terry_Athletic_Field" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles H. Terry Athletic Field">Charles H. Terry Athletic Park</a> on Lolita Tizol Street, just north of the entrance to Historic Ponce at Puente de los Leones (Lions\' Bridge) and the <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Tricentennial_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Ponce Tricentennial Park">Ponce Tricentennial Park</a>. In 2012 the city commenced construction of the multi-sport complex <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Deportiva_Millito_Navarro" title="Ciudad Deportiva Millito Navarro">Ciudad Deportiva Millito Navarro</a>. No date has been announced for its completion yet, but its <a href="/wiki/Skateboarding" title="Skateboarding">skateboarding</a> section opened in March 2013.\n</p><p>The main annual sports events are as follows:\n</p>\n<ul><li>April \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Las_Justas" title="Las Justas">Las Justas</a> \xe2\x80\x93 intercollegiate sports competition</li>\n<li>May \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Grand_Prix" class="mw-redirect" title="Ponce Grand Prix">Ponce Grand Prix</a> \xe2\x80\x93 international track and field competition</li>\n<li>August \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Cruce_a_Nado_Internacional" title="Cruce a Nado Internacional">Cruce a Nado Internacional</a> \xe2\x80\x93 international swimming competition</li>\n<li>December \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Marathon" title="Ponce Marathon">Marat\xc3\xb3n La Guadalupe\xe2\x80\x93</a> - 26-mile national marathon</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Recreation">Recreation</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Recreation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_parks_in_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of parks in Ponce, Puerto Rico">List of parks in Ponce, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_beaches_in_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of beaches in Ponce, Puerto Rico">List of beaches in Ponce, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ponce_La_Guancha_Beach.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Ponce_La_Guancha_Beach.jpg/200px-Ponce_La_Guancha_Beach.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Ponce_La_Guancha_Beach.jpg/300px-Ponce_La_Guancha_Beach.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Ponce_La_Guancha_Beach.jpg/400px-Ponce_La_Guancha_Beach.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a><figcaption>La Guancha Beach at <a href="/wiki/La_Guancha_Boardwalk" class="mw-redirect" title="La Guancha Boardwalk">La Guancha</a>, one of 40 salt-water beaches in Ponce</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The municipality is home to several parks and beaches, including both passive and active parks. Among the most popular passive parks are the <a href="/wiki/Julio_Enrique_Monagas_Family_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Julio Enrique Monagas Family Park">Julio Enrique Monagas Family Park</a> on Ponce By-pass Road (<a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_2" title="Puerto Rico Highway 2">PR-2</a>) at the location where the Rio Portugu\xc3\xa9s feeds into <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Bucan%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="R\xc3\xado Bucan\xc3\xa1">Bucan\xc3\xa1</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Dora_Col%C3%B3n_Clavell_Urban_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Dora Col\xc3\xb3n Clavell Urban Park">Parque Urbano Dora Colon Clavell</a>, another passive park is in the downtown area. Active parks include the Charles H. Terry Athletic Field, and several municipal tennis courts, including one at Poly Deportivos with 9 hard courts, and one at La Rambla with six hard courts.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>237<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There are also many public basketball courts scattered throughout the various barrios of the municipality.\n</p><p>The municipality has 40 beaches including 28 on the mainland and 12 in Caja de Muertos.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>238<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Among these, about a dozen of them are most notable, including <a href="/wiki/El_Tuque" title="El Tuque">El Tuque</a> Beach in the <a href="/wiki/El_Tuque" title="El Tuque">El Tuque</a> sector on highway PR-2, west of the city, <a href="/wiki/Paseo_Tablado_La_Guancha" title="Paseo Tablado La Guancha">La Guancha Beach</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Complejo_Recreativo_y_Cultural_La_Guancha" title="Complejo Recreativo y Cultural La Guancha">La Guancha</a> sector south of the city, and four beaches in <a href="/wiki/Caja_de_Muertos,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Caja de Muertos, Puerto Rico">Caja de Muertos</a>: Pelicano, Playa Larga, Carrucho, and Coast Guard beach.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>239<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferry</a> must be boarded at La Guancha for transportation to the Caja de Muertos beaches.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Religion">Religion</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Religion"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>During and after colonization, the Roman Catholic Church became the established religion of the colony. Gradually African slaves were converted to Christianity, but many incorporated their own traditions and symbols, maintaining African traditions as well. <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="Ponce Cathedral">Ponce Cathedral</a>, listed in the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>, was built in 1839.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>240<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>241<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Royal Decree of Graces of 1815 allowed for non-Catholics to immigrate legally to Puerto Rico, but it required those who wanted to settle on the island to make a vow of alliance to the Catholic Church. Ponce was the first city in Puerto Rico where <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> churches were built.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>242<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Centro_Islamico_de_Ponce,_Bo_Cuarto,_Ponce,_PR_(IMG_3392).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Centro_Islamico_de_Ponce%2C_Bo_Cuarto%2C_Ponce%2C_PR_%28IMG_3392%29.jpg/200px-Centro_Islamico_de_Ponce%2C_Bo_Cuarto%2C_Ponce%2C_PR_%28IMG_3392%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Centro_Islamico_de_Ponce%2C_Bo_Cuarto%2C_Ponce%2C_PR_%28IMG_3392%29.jpg/300px-Centro_Islamico_de_Ponce%2C_Bo_Cuarto%2C_Ponce%2C_PR_%28IMG_3392%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Centro_Islamico_de_Ponce%2C_Bo_Cuarto%2C_Ponce%2C_PR_%28IMG_3392%29.jpg/400px-Centro_Islamico_de_Ponce%2C_Bo_Cuarto%2C_Ponce%2C_PR_%28IMG_3392%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024" /></a><figcaption>Islamic Center at Ponce: numerous religious faiths are practiced in the city</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Methodist_Church_on_Villa_Street,_Barrio_Segundo,_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico_(IMG_2874).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Methodist_Church_on_Villa_Street%2C_Barrio_Segundo%2C_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico_%28IMG_2874%29.jpg/220px-Methodist_Church_on_Villa_Street%2C_Barrio_Segundo%2C_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico_%28IMG_2874%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Methodist_Church_on_Villa_Street%2C_Barrio_Segundo%2C_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico_%28IMG_2874%29.jpg/330px-Methodist_Church_on_Villa_Street%2C_Barrio_Segundo%2C_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico_%28IMG_2874%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Methodist_Church_on_Villa_Street%2C_Barrio_Segundo%2C_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico_%28IMG_2874%29.jpg/440px-Methodist_Church_on_Villa_Street%2C_Barrio_Segundo%2C_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico_%28IMG_2874%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a><figcaption>The 1907 <a href="/wiki/Primera_Iglesia_Metodista_Unida_de_Ponce" title="Primera Iglesia Metodista Unida de Ponce">Methodist Church in Ponce</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>With the U.S. invasion, there was a significant change in the religious landscape in the City and in Puerto Rico. "The Protestant missionaries followed the footprints of the United States soldiers, right after the Treaty of Paris was ratified and Puerto Rico was ceded to the American government."<sup id="cite_ref-Aida_Belen_Rivera_Ruiz_2008._Page_20_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aida_Belen_Rivera_Ruiz_2008._Page_20-250"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>243<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By March 1899, eight months after the occupation, executives from the <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist Church">Methodists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_(United_States)" title="Episcopal Church (United States)">Episcopalians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">Baptists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterian Church">Presbyterians</a>, and others, had arranged for an evangelical division whereby Ponce would have Evangelical, Baptist, and Methodist "campaigns". With the passing of the <a href="/wiki/Foraker_Act" title="Foraker Act">Foraker Act</a> in 1900, which established total separation between Church and State, the absolute power of the Catholic Church eroded quickly.<sup id="cite_ref-Aida_Belen_Rivera_Ruiz_2008._Page_20_250-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aida_Belen_Rivera_Ruiz_2008._Page_20-250"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>243<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Various Protestant churches were soon established and built in Ponce; today many are recognized as historic sites. Among them are the <a href="/wiki/McCabe_Memorial_Church" title="McCabe Memorial Church">McCabe Memorial Church</a> (Methodist) (1908),<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>244<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Primera_Iglesia_Metodista_Unida_de_Ponce" title="Primera Iglesia Metodista Unida de Ponce">Missionary Society of the Methodist Episcopal Church</a> (Methodist) (1907).<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>245<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The bell of the Episcopalian <a href="/wiki/Iglesia_de_la_Santisima_Trinidad" class="mw-redirect" title="Iglesia de la Santisima Trinidad">Holy Trinity Church</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cuarto_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cuarto (Ponce)">Barrio Cuarto</a>, rang again<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>246<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> when the Americans arrived on 25 July 1898. Built in 1873, the church was allowed to function by the Spanish Crown under the conditions that its bell would not be rung, its front doors would always remain closed, and its services would be offered in English only.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>247<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>\nToday, Ponce is home to a mix of religious faiths: both Protestants and Catholics, as well as <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a>, have places of worship in Ponce. Baptists, Methodists, Presbyterians, Episcopalians, <a href="/wiki/Assemblies_of_God_USA" title="Assemblies of God USA">Pentecostals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Adventists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Synod_of_North_America" title="Evangelical Synod of North America">Evangelicals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disciples_of_Christ" class="mw-redirect" title="Disciples of Christ">Disciples of Christ</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Congregational_church" class="mw-redirect" title="Congregational church">Congregationalists</a> are among the Protestant faiths with a following in Ponce. Catholicism is the faith of the majority of <i>ponce\xc3\xb1os.</i> In 2009, the Catholic Church had 18 parishes in the municipality, two bishops and 131 priests.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>248<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In his <i>Memoirs</i>, Albert E. Lee summed up Ponce\'s attitude towards religion:<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1244412712">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 32px}.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;margin-top:0}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .templatequotecite{padding-left:1.6em}}</style></p><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Ponce was not only tolerant, it was indifferent in religious matters. Protestants and Catholics, and even atheists, lived together socially on the friendliest terms. Religion was strictly a personal affair in Ponce while in San Juan at times gave the impression that it was ready to practice the <a href="/wiki/Auto-da-f%C3%A9" title="Auto-da-f\xc3\xa9">auto-de-fe</a> [sic]."<i><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>249<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></i></p></blockquote>\n<div style="clear:both;" class=""></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Banco_Popular_in_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Banco_Popular_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Banco_Popular_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Banco_Popular_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Banco_Popular_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Banco_Popular_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Banco_Popular_in_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1360" /></a><figcaption>Before its merger with <a href="/wiki/Popular,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Popular, Inc.">Banco Popular</a> in 1991, <a href="/wiki/Banco_de_Ponce" title="Banco de Ponce">Banco de Ponce</a> (above) had the most extensive international network of branches of any Puerto Rican bank<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>250<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></figcaption></figure>\n<p>Traditionally the city\'s economy had depended almost entirely on the sugarcane industry.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>251<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Since around the 1950s, however, the town\'s economy has diversified and today its economy revolves around a mixed-industry manufacturing sector, retail, and tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>252<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>253<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The building of a <a href="/wiki/Port_of_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Port of the Americas">mega port</a>, anticipated to be completed in 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>254<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is expected to add significantly to the area\'s economy. Agriculture, retail, and services are also significant players in the local economy. It is considered an agricultural, trade, and distribution center, with manufacturing that includes electronics, communications equipment, food processing, pharmaceutical drugs, concrete plants, scientific instruments and rum distilling as well as an established gourmet coffee agricultural industry.<sup id="cite_ref-thinkponce.com_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thinkponce.com-262"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>255<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The city, though, suffers from an unemployment rate that hovers around the 15 percent mark.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>256<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Manufacturing">Manufacturing</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Manufacturing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The municipality is considered one of the most developed municipalities in Puerto Rico.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>257<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a> sectors include <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electrical" class="mw-redirect" title="Electrical">electrical</a> equipment, <a href="/wiki/Communications" class="mw-redirect" title="Communications">communications</a> equipment, <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">food processing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_drug" class="mw-redirect" title="Pharmaceutical drug">pharmaceutical drugs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Concrete_plant" title="Concrete plant">concrete plants</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Scientific_instrument" title="Scientific instrument">scientific instruments</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thinkponce.com_262-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thinkponce.com-262"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>255<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It also produces <a href="/wiki/Leather_goods" class="mw-redirect" title="Leather goods">leather products</a>, <a href="/wiki/Needlework" title="Needlework">needlework</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a> <a href="/wiki/Flour" title="Flour">flour</a> to a lesser extent. Ponce is home to the <a href="/wiki/Destiler%C3%ADa_Serrall%C3%A9s" title="Destiler\xc3\xada Serrall\xc3\xa9s">Serralles</a> rum distillery, which manufactures <a href="/wiki/Don_Q" title="Don Q">Don Q</a>, and to <a href="/wiki/Industrias_Vassallo" title="Industrias Vassallo">Industrias Vassallo</a>, a leader in <a href="/wiki/PVC" class="mw-redirect" title="PVC">PVC</a> manufacturing. Other important local manufacturers are <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Cement,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Ponce Cement, Inc.">Ponce Cement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cristalia_Premium_Water" title="Cristalia Premium Water">Cristalia Premium Water</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rovira_Biscuits_Corporation" title="Rovira Biscuits Corporation">Rovira Biscuits Corporation</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Caf%C3%A9_Rico" title="Caf\xc3\xa9 Rico">Caf\xc3\xa9 Rico</a>. Ponce was once the headquarters for <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Iron_Works" title="Puerto Rico Iron Works">Puerto Rico Iron Works</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Salt_Industries" title="Ponce Salt Industries">Ponce Salt Industries</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Candy_Industries" title="Ponce Candy Industries">Ponce Candy Industries</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Agriculture">Agriculture</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Agriculture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>In the agricultural sector, the most important products are <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, followed by <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banana" title="Banana">bananas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_(fruit)" title="Orange (fruit)">oranges</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Grapefruit" title="Grapefruit">grapefruits</a>. A mix of public and private services, as well as finance, retail sales, and construction round up Ponce\'s economic rhythm.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>258<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cafe_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Cafe Rico">Cafe Rico</a>, which metamorphosed from coffee-grower Cafeteros de Puerto Rico, has its headquarters in Ponce.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Retail">Retail</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Retail"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Paseo_Atocha_Promenade_2.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Paseo_Atocha_Promenade_2.jpg/200px-Paseo_Atocha_Promenade_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Paseo_Atocha_Promenade_2.jpg/300px-Paseo_Atocha_Promenade_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Paseo_Atocha_Promenade_2.jpg/400px-Paseo_Atocha_Promenade_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="333" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Paseo_Atocha" title="Paseo Atocha">Atocha Promenade</a> is part of <i>El Ponce Tradicional</i>, the old historic district</figcaption></figure>\n<p>For many years commercial retail activity in Ponce centered around what is now <a href="/wiki/Paseo_Atocha" title="Paseo Atocha">Paseo Atocha</a>. This has shifted in recent years, and most retail activity today occurs in one of Ponce\'s various <a href="/wiki/Shopping_mall" title="Shopping mall">malls</a>, in particular <a href="/wiki/Plaza_del_Caribe" title="Plaza del Caribe">Plaza del Caribe</a>. <a href="/wiki/Centro_del_Sur_Mall" title="Centro del Sur Mall">Centro del Sur Mall</a> is also a significant retail area, as is Ponce Mall.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>259<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Mega_port">Mega port</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Mega port"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Ponce is home to Puerto Rico\'s chief Caribbean port, the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Ponce" class="mw-redirect" title="Port of Ponce">Port of Ponce</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>260<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The port is expanding to transform it into a mega port, called the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Port of the Americas">Port of the Americas</a> that will operate as an international transshipment port. When fully operational, it is expected to support 100,000 jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>261<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Demographics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Demographics of Puerto Rico">Demographics of Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236656977">.mw-parser-output .mw-parser-output .cs1-maint{color:#18911f}}@media screen and (prefers-color-scheme:dark){html.skin-theme-clientpref-os .mw-parser-output .cs1-maint{color:#18911f}}</style><cite class="citation web
