Census Bureau</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">July 13,</span> 2006</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=U.S.+Census+website&amp;rft.pub=United+States+Census+Bureau&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.census.gov&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APonce%2C+Puerto+Rico" class="Z3988"></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table class="wikitable floatright">\n<caption><b>Racial distribution</b>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="3">Race - Ponce, Puerto Rico - 2020 Census<sup id="cite_ref-factfinder.census.gov_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factfinder.census.gov-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Race\n</th>\n<th>Population\n</th>\n<th>% of Total\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/White_people" title="White people">White</a></b></td>\n<td>26,148</td>\n<td>19.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Black/Afro Puerto Rican</b></td>\n<td>18,325</td>\n<td>13.3%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">American Indian</a>/Alaska Native</b></td>\n<td>4,129</td>\n<td>3.0%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b><a href="/wiki/Asian_people" title="Asian people">Asian</a></b></td>\n<td>365</td>\n<td>0.3%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>Two or more races/Some other race</b></td>\n<td>88,524</td>\n<td>64.4%\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Ponce has consistently ranked as one of the most populous cities in Puerto Rico. Ponce\'s population, according to the 2010 census, stands at 166,327, with a <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> of 1,449.3 persons&#160;per square mile (559.6 persons/km<sup>2</sup>), ranking third in terms of population among <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rican</a> municipalities. As of 2000, speakers of <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> as a first language accounted for 13.89% of the population. <sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>263<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of mayors of Ponce, Puerto Rico">List of mayors of Ponce, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ponce_City_Hall.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Ponce_City_Hall.JPG/220px-Ponce_City_Hall.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Ponce_City_Hall.JPG/330px-Ponce_City_Hall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Ponce_City_Hall.JPG/440px-Ponce_City_Hall.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Ponce_City_Hall" title="Ponce City Hall">Ponce Municipal Hall</a>, built in the 1840s, is the oldest <a href="/wiki/Colonial_architecture" title="Colonial architecture">colonial</a> building in the city.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Municipal_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipal government">municipal government</a> has its seat in the city of Ponce.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>264<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>265<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Since its foundation in 1692, the city of Ponce has been led by a <a href="/wiki/Mayor" title="Mayor">mayor</a>. Its first mayor was <a href="/wiki/Pedro_S%C3%A1nchez_de_Mathos" title="Pedro S\xc3\xa1nchez de Mathos">Don Pedro S\xc3\xa1nchez de Matos</a>. The <a href="/wiki/2008_Puerto_Rican_general_election" title="2008 Puerto Rican general election">2008 election</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Mel%C3%A9ndez" title="Mar\xc3\xada Mel\xc3\xa9ndez">Mar\xc3\xada Mel\xc3\xa9ndez Altieri</a> (<a href="/wiki/New_Progressive_Party_(Puerto_Rico)" title="New Progressive Party (Puerto Rico)">PNP</a>), brought Ponce the first woman to be elected to the mayoral office in the city\'s history. She was re-elected in <a href="/wiki/2012_Puerto_Rican_general_election" title="2012 Puerto Rican general election">2012</a> and again in <a href="/wiki/2016_Puerto_Rican_general_election" title="2016 Puerto Rican general election">2016</a>, and serve as mayor until 2021. In the <a href="/wiki/2020_Puerto_Rican_general_election" title="2020 Puerto Rican general election">2020</a> election <a href="/wiki/Luis_Irizarry_Pab%C3%B3n" title="Luis Irizarry Pab\xc3\xb3n">Luis Irizarri Pab\xc3\xb3n</a> (<a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Popular Democratic Party (Puerto Rico)">PPD</a>) was elected as mayor and is currently serving as mayor.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>266<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Ponce\'s best known <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of mayors of Ponce, Puerto Rico">mayor</a> of recent years is perhaps <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Cordero_Santiago" title="Rafael Cordero Santiago">Rafael "Churumba" Cordero Santiago</a> (<a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Popular Democratic Party (Puerto Rico)">PPD</a>), who held office from 1989 until his sudden death on the morning of 17 January 2004, after suffering three successive brain strokes.\n</p><p>The city also has a municipal legislature that handles local <a href="/wiki/Legislative" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative">legislative</a> matters. Ponce has had a municipal council since 1812.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>267<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>f<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>268<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The municipal legislature is composed of 16 civilians elected during the general elections, along with the mayor, state representatives and senators. The delegations are, until the 2020 general election, distributed as follows: 13 legislators of the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Popular Democratic Party (Puerto Rico)">Popular Democratic Party</a>, two legislators of the <a href="/wiki/New_Progressive_Party_(Puerto_Rico)" title="New Progressive Party (Puerto Rico)">New Progressive Party</a>, and one legislator from the <a href="/wiki/Movimiento_Victoria_Ciudadana" title="Movimiento Victoria Ciudadana">Movimento Victoria Ciudadana</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ponce_City_Hall" title="Ponce City Hall">Ponce City Hall</a> has one of the most unusual histories of any city hall throughout the world. "Originally built in the 1840s as a public assembly hall, Ponce\'s City Hall was a jail until the end of the 19th century. Current galleries were former cells, and executions were held in the courtyard. Four U.S. presidents spoke from the balcony - Theodore Roosevelt, Herbert Hoover, Franklin Roosevelt and George Bush." It is listed in the <a href="/wiki/National_Register_of_Historic_Places" title="National Register of Historic Places">National Register of Historic Places</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>269<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2005, the municipality\'s budget was US$152 million.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>270<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2010-2011 it was $158 million.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>271<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2016-2017 the proposed budget was $140 million.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>272<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> From a business perspective, the Ponce municipal government is generally praised for its efficiency and speediness, thanks to its adoption of the Autonomous Municipality Law of 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>273<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The municipality of Ponce is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_V" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district V">Puerto Rico Senatorial district V</a>, which is represented by two senators. During the <a href="/wiki/2020_Puerto_Rico_Senate_election" title="2020 Puerto Rico Senate election">2020 Puerto Rico Senate election</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marially_Gonz%C3%A1lez_Huertas" title="Marially Gonz\xc3\xa1lez Huertas">Marially Gonz\xc3\xa1lez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Ruiz" title="Ram\xc3\xb3n Ruiz">Ram\xc3\xb3n Ruiz</a>, both from the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_(Puerto_Rico)" title="Popular Democratic Party (Puerto Rico)">Popular Democratic Party</a>, were elected as District Senators and are currently serving.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>274<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>275<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> of the municipality is based on the design of the official mayoral seal that was adopted in 1844 under the administration of mayor <a href="/wiki/Salvador_de_Vives" title="Salvador de Vives">Salvador de Vives</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-visitponce.com_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitponce.com-284"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>276<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The coat of arms of Ponce consists of an <a href="/wiki/Escutcheon_(heraldry)" title="Escutcheon (heraldry)">escutcheon</a> (shield) in the <a href="/wiki/Escutcheon_(heraldry)#Points" title="Escutcheon (heraldry)">Spanish</a> tradition. This shield has a <a href="/wiki/Field_(heraldry)" title="Field (heraldry)">field</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Heraldry#Divisions_of_the_field" title="Heraldry">party per bend</a> division. The division runs from top left to bottom right. The field is red and black, bordered with a fine golden line. In the center of the shield is the figure of an erect lion standing on a bridge. The top of the bridge is a golden, the middle is red bricks, and the base foundation is gray rocks. Under the bridge there are gray wavy lines. Over the shield rests a five-tower golden stone wall with openings in the form of red windows. To the left of the shield is a coffee tree branch with its fruit, and to the right of the shield is a sugarcane stalk. The symbols of the shield are as follows: The field represents the flag of the municipality of Ponce, divided diagonally in the traditional city colors: red and black. The lion over the bridge alludes to the last name of the conqueror and first governor of Puerto Rico, Juan Ponce de Leon. The waves under the bridge allude to the Rio Portugues, on the banks of which the city was born. The <a href="/wiki/Coronet" title="Coronet">coronet</a> in the form of a five-tower mural crown above the shield allude to the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish crown">Spanish crown</a>, through which the settlement obtained its city charter. The coffee tree branch and the sugarcane stalk represent the main agricultural basis of the economy of the young municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-visitponce.com_284-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visitponce.com-284"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>276<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag">Flag</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1237032888/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Bandera_de_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Bandera_de_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg/200px-Bandera_de_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="121" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Bandera_de_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg/300px-Bandera_de_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Bandera_de_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg/400px-Bandera_de_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="790" data-file-height="476" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">The 1692 Flag of the Municipality of Ponce, adopted in 1967, commemorates its founding</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico_-_1877_version.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Flag_of_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_1877_version.svg/200px-Flag_of_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_1877_version.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="121" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Flag_of_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_1877_version.svg/300px-Flag_of_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_1877_version.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Flag_of_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_1877_version.svg/400px-Flag_of_Ponce%2C_Puerto_Rico_-_1877_version.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="790" data-file-height="476" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">The 1877 Flag of the city of Ponce, adopted in 1977, commemorates the year of its city charter</div></div></div></div></div>\n<p>Ponce has two official flags, one for the municipality and one for the city proper. The municipal flag, "the 1692 flag", was adopted in 1967 via a <a href="/wiki/Municipal_ordinance" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipal ordinance">municipal ordinance</a>. This flag, designed by Mario Ramirez, was selected from among a number of public proposals. It consisted of a rectangular cloth divided by a diagonal line into two equal <a href="/wiki/Triangle#Types_of_triangle" title="Triangle">isosceles triangles</a>. The line ran from the top right-hand corner to the bottom left-hand corner. The top triangle was black; the bottom right triangle was red. On the top triangle was the figure of a lion over a bridge. On the bottom triangle was the word "Ponce" with the number "1692", the date when the municipality was founded. Ponce Municipal Assembly Order No. 5, Section 5, of Municipal Assembly Year 1966-1967 established that the last Sunday in April is "D\xc3\xada de la Bandera de Ponce" (Ponce Flag Day).<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>277<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Ten years later, in 1977, a new municipal ordinance introduced a flag, "the 1877 city flag" to commemorate the 100th anniversary of the declaration of the <i>city</i> charter. This (1977) flag consisted of a rectangular cloth divided by a diagonal line, creating two equal isosceles triangles, starting from the top left hand corner and ending on the lower right hand corner. The top triangle is red; the bottom triangle is black. In the center of the flag sits the shield of the municipality. Under this shield is the number "1877", the year of the founding of the city, and above the shield is the word "PONCE". Some flags have the "1877" date on the left border of the bottom triangle and the name of the city on the right border of the triangle, as illustrated in the insert on the left.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>278<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;" class=""></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Municipal_services">Municipal services</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Municipal services"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Fire_protection">Fire protection</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Fire protection"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Parque_de_Bombas-Ponce_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Parque_de_Bombas-Ponce_Puerto_Rico.jpg/200px-Parque_de_Bombas-Ponce_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="267" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Parque_de_Bombas-Ponce_Puerto_Rico.jpg/300px-Parque_de_Bombas-Ponce_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Parque_de_Bombas-Ponce_Puerto_Rico.jpg/400px-Parque_de_Bombas-Ponce_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="800" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Parque_de_Bombas" title="Parque de Bombas">Parque de Bombas</a> - Long the iconic symbol of the city, was the first fire station in Puerto Rico</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The city\'s fire department has a history of firsts, including being the first organized fire department in the Island. As the largest city in the island at the time, and <i>de facto</i> economic and social center of Puerto Rico, this in effect also created the first <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Fire_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Fire Department">Puerto Rico Fire Department</a>. The Ponce Fire Department also built the first fire station in the Island,<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>279<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>280<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> which still stands to this day, and is now open as the <a href="/wiki/Parque_de_Bombas" title="Parque de Bombas">Parque de Bombas</a> museum. Also, in 1951, Ponce\'s Fire Chief <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_G%C3%A1ndara_Cartagena" title="Ra\xc3\xbal G\xc3\xa1ndara Cartagena">Ra\xc3\xbal G\xc3\xa1ndara Cartagena</a>, wrote a book on the firemen\'s service, which became a firemen\'s manual in several Latin American countries.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>281<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In recognition of the service rendered by its fire fighters, the City of Ponce built them homes resulting in the creation of the <a href="/wiki/25_de_Enero_Street" class="mw-redirect" title="25 de Enero Street">25 de Enero Street</a> near the city\'s historic district.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Major_fires">Major fires</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Major fires"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The city has withstood some nearly catastrophic fires.\n</p><p>A major fire took place on February 27, 1820,<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>282<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>283<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> that "almost destroyed the early Ponce settlement". It destroyed 106 "of the best homes in town."<sup id="cite_ref-Ponce._1913._Page_194_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ponce._1913._Page_194-292"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>284<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1823, then Governor of Puerto Rico, <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_la_Torre" title="Miguel de la Torre">Miguel de la Torre</a> mandated that "every male from 16 to 60 years old must be a firefighter".<sup id="cite_ref-bomberos.gobierno.pr_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bomberos.gobierno.pr-293"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>285<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Those firefighters had to supply their own fire fighting equipment (essentially picks, buckets, and shovels). Once De la Torre left office, this first fire fighting institution started to decay.<sup id="cite_ref-bomberos.gobierno.pr_293-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bomberos.gobierno.pr-293"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>285<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Another major fire occurred in <a href="/wiki/La_Playa_(de_Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="La Playa (de Ponce)">La Playa</a> in March 1845,<sup id="cite_ref-Ponce._1913._Page_194_292-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ponce._1913._Page_194-292"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>284<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> that destroyed "most of the Ponce vicinity." It significantly damaged the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Custom_House_(Ponce,_Puerto_Rico)" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Custom House (Ponce, Puerto Rico)">Spanish Customs House in Ponce</a>, this being one of the few buildings left standing after the fire.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>286<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The fire burned down the major buildings of the "Marina de Ponce".<sup id="cite_ref-Ponce._1913._Page_194_292-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ponce._1913._Page_194-292"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>284<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After this fire, then governor of Puerto Rico Conde de Mirasol (born Rafael de Aristegui y Velez),<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>287<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> created a new fire fighting organization staffed by volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-bomberos.gobierno.pr_293-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bomberos.gobierno.pr-293"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>285<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1862, the Ponce Firefighters Corps was reorganized under the administration of Ponce mayor <a href="/wiki/Luis_de_Quixano_y_Font" title="Luis de Quixano y Font">Luis de Quixano y Font</a>, and Tom\xc3\xa1s Cladellas was named fire chief.<sup id="cite_ref-bomberos.gobierno.pr_293-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bomberos.gobierno.pr-293"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>285<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1879 the Ponce Fire Corps reorganized again, with a new fire chief, the local architect <a href="/wiki/Juan_Bertoli_Calderoni" title="Juan Bertoli Calderoni">Juan Bertoli</a>.\n</p><p>On September 25, 1880 another fire, took place destroying most of the older civil records (births, baptisms, marriages, etc.) of the Ponce parish.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>288<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1883, the Ponce firefighter corps reorganized once more, this time in a more definitive fashion when <a href="/wiki/Maximo_de_Meana_y_Guridi" class="mw-redirect" title="Maximo de Meana y Guridi">M\xc3\xa1ximo Meana</a> was mayor of Ponce. During this time the Ponce Fire Corps was made up of 400 firefighters. Its leadership consisted of Julio Steinacher, fire chief, Juan Seix, second fire chief, Oscar Schuch Olivero, Chief of Brigade, and Fernando M. Toro, Supervisor of the Gymnastics Academy. Concurrent with this, the firefighter corps music band was organized. In September 1883, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Morel_Campos" title="Juan Morel Campos">Juan Morel Campos</a> formally organized the Ponce Fire Corps Municipal Band which exists to this day.<sup id="cite_ref-bomberos.gobierno.pr_293-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bomberos.gobierno.pr-293"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>285<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Calle_25_de_Enero.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Calle_25_de_Enero.jpg/200px-Calle_25_de_Enero.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Calle_25_de_Enero.jpg/300px-Calle_25_de_Enero.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Calle_25_de_Enero.jpg/400px-Calle_25_de_Enero.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a><figcaption>Distinctive red-and-black striped cottages at <a href="/wiki/Calle_25_de_Enero" title="Calle 25 de Enero">Calle 25 de Enero</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>The fourth Ponce fire of large proportions occurred on January 25, 1899.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>289<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The fire was fought by a group of firefighters among whom was Pedro Sabater and the civilian <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Rivera_Esbr%C3%AD" title="Rafael Rivera Esbr\xc3\xad">Rafael Rivera Esbr\xc3\xad</a>, who would later become mayor of the city. The fire started at the U.S. munitions depot on the lot currently occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Ponce_High_School" title="Ponce High School">Ponce High School</a> building and grounds. The heroes in that fire, believed to have saved the city from certain annihilation, are remembered to this day with monuments on their tombs as well as in a monument in the city square <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Las_Delicias" title="Plaza Las Delicias">Plaza Las Delicias</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bomberos.gobierno.pr_293-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bomberos.gobierno.pr-293"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>285<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As a further gesture of gratitude, a neighborhood of distinctive Victorian-style cottages were constructed to house the firefighters and their families. These houses, painted in the red and black colors of the city, are located along a street named <a href="/wiki/Calle_25_de_Enero" title="Calle 25 de Enero">Calle 25 de Enero</a> (<i>25 de Enero street</i>); they are still owned and occupied by the descendants of these firefighters and are a scenic attraction in Ponce\'s historic center.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Police">Police</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Police"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ponce_Municipal_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="Ponce Municipal Police">Ponce Municipal Police</a> consists of a force of some 500 officers.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>290<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This force is complemented by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Police" title="Puerto Rico Police">Puerto Rico Police</a> force. The Ponce Municipal Police has its headquarters at the southwest corner of the intersection of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_163" title="Puerto Rico Highway 163">PR-163</a> (<a href="/wiki/Canas_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Canas (Ponce)">Las Americas Avenue</a>) and PR-2R (Carretera P\xc3\xa1mpanos). In addition it has three precincts as follows: <a href="/wiki/Quinto_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Quinto (Ponce)">Cantera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paseo_Tablado_La_Guancha" title="Paseo Tablado La Guancha">La Guancha</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Coto_Laurel" title="Coto Laurel">Coto Laurel</a>, plus specialized units at <a href="/wiki/Port_of_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Port of the Americas">Port of the Americas</a> (maritime unit), <a href="/wiki/Canas_Urbano" title="Canas Urbano">Mariani</a> (transit unit), <a href="/wiki/Segundo_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Segundo (Ponce)">Belgica</a> (motorcycle unit), and <a href="/wiki/Primero_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Primero (Ponce)">Parque Dora Clavell</a> (tourism unit).\n</p><p>The Puerto Rico Police had its Ponce area regional headquarters from 1970 until 2011 on Hostos Avenue.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>291<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2011 it moved its command center to a new and larger facility further west on Urbanizacion Los Caobos in Barrio <a href="/wiki/Bucana" class="mw-redirect" title="Bucana">Bucana</a>. It commands five precincts in the city: <a href="/wiki/Canas_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Canas (Ponce)">Villa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Playa_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Playa (Ponce)">Playa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Magueyes_Urbano" title="Magueyes Urbano">Morel Campos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machuelo_Abajo" title="Machuelo Abajo">La Rambla</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Canas_(Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Canas (Ponce)">El Tuque</a>. The Ponce municipal coverage of the Puerto Rico Police force is as follows:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The Villa precinct covers barrios Primero, Segundo, Tercero, Cuarto, Quinto, and Sexto, and Portugu\xc3\xa9s Urbano. This precinct includes the historic Ponce district.</li>\n<li>The Playa precinct (# 258<sup id="cite_ref-Home_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Home-300"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>292<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>) covers the barrios of Playa, Capitanejo, Bucan\xc3\xa1, and Vayas.</li>\n<li>The La Rambla precinct covers barrios An\xc3\xb3n, Real, Marag\xc3\xbcez, Cerrillos, Coto Laurel, Sabanetas, San Patricio, Monte Llano, Machuelo Arriba, Machuelo Abajo, and Portugu\xc3\xa9s.</li>\n<li>The El Tuque precinct covers barrios Canas and Canas Urbano.</li>\n<li>The Morel Campos precinct covers barrios Guaraguao, Marue\xc3\xb1o, Tibes, Magueyes, Magueyes Urbano, and Quebrada Lim\xc3\xb3n.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Crime">Crime</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Crime"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>In 2002, most of the homicides in Puerto Rico were occurring in San Juan and the greater metropolitan areas of Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Carolina and Caguas, but Ponce also had a high homicide rate. Also in 2002, Puerto Rico law enforcement officials drafted plans to increase the number of forensic investigators by 25%. The investigators, assigned to the Institute of Forensic Sciences in San Juan, covered homicides in about 65 percent of the island, but the Institute was considering assigning Ponce its own unit.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>293<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By mid-year 2005, there had been 25 more murder cases in Ponce than for all of 2004, a significant increase.<sup id="cite_ref-Puerto_Rico_Herald._14_July_2005_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Puerto_Rico_Herald._14_July_2005-302"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>294<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The police acknowledged that most crime cases in Puerto Rico are linked to drug-trafficking and illegal weapons. In mid-July 2005, Gov. <a href="/wiki/An%C3%ADbal_Acevedo_Vil%C3%A1" title="An\xc3\xadbal Acevedo Vil\xc3\xa1">An\xc3\xadbal Acevedo Vil\xc3\xa1</a> announced a series of measures aimed at lowering Ponce\'s high murder rate. Some of those measures included the permanent transfer of 100 agents to the area, the appointment of a ballistics expert from the Institute of Forensic Sciences and of two prosecutors for the Department of Justice in Ponce. Puerto Rico Police Superintendent <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Toledo" title="Pedro Toledo">Pedro Toledo</a> admitted that more than 100 agents are actually needed in the Ponce region in 2005, but that "there would be no additional transfers at the moment to avoid affecting other police areas."<sup id="cite_ref-Puerto_Rico_Herald._14_July_2005_302-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Puerto_Rico_Herald._14_July_2005-302"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>294<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Ponce is a convenient transition point for drug smugglers due to its location on the Caribbean Sea and its proximity to <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Intensity_Drug_Trafficking_Area_Page_5_303-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Intensity_Drug_Trafficking_Area_Page_5-303"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>295<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> From there packages are then transported to the United States by various means including the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">United States Postal Service</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Intensity_Drug_Trafficking_Area_Page_5_303-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Intensity_Drug_Trafficking_Area_Page_5-303"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>295<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The city is included in the area\'s <a href="/wiki/HIDTA" class="mw-redirect" title="HIDTA">HIDTA</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-Intensity_Drug_Trafficking_Area_Page_5_303-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Intensity_Drug_Trafficking_Area_Page_5-303"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>295<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>As most of the crime in Ponce is connected to the drug-trade, police have an eye on illegal smuggling through the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Ponce" class="mw-redirect" title="Port of Ponce">Port of Ponce</a><sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>296<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A 2008 government report stated that, "Drug smuggling in containerized cargo is a significant maritime threat to the HIDTA (High Intensity Drug Trafficking Area) region. The vast and increasing quantity of goods transshipped through the region every year provides drug traffickers with ample opportunity to smuggle illicit drugs into, through, and from the area.<sup id="cite_ref-Intensity_Drug_Trafficking_Area_Page_5_303-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Intensity_Drug_Trafficking_Area_Page_5-303"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>295<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In July 2005, local police scored some points in their fight against drug-trafficking.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>297<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>By 2007, Ponce had experienced a 61% decline in the rate of violent crimes (<i>Type I</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>298<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2010, there was a further reduction of 12 percent in violent crimes over 2009 statistics.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>299<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In August 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Police#Ponce" title="Puerto Rico Police">Ponce Area Police Region</a>, which includes Ponce and seven other adjacent municipalities, registered 27 fewer Type I crimes that it had by the same period in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>300<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>For the Ponce <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Metropolitan Statistical Area">MSA</a>, <i>which includes the city of Ponce, its nineteen surrounding municipal barrios, the municipality of Juana Diaz, and the municipality of Villalba</i>, crime data was tabulated in 2002 (Total MSA Population: 364,849). No data is available for the city or for the municipality of Ponce alone. The following statistics are registered:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Category\n</th>\n<th>Number\n</th>\n<th>Rate per 100,000\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Violent vehicle theft</i>\n</td>\n<td>547\n</td>\n<td>149.9\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p><small>\nNotes:<br />\n^ Violent crimes include: murder, forcible rape, robbery, and aggravated assault. <br title="FBI">FBI</a><sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>301<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></small>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="FBI_satellite_office">FBI satellite office</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: FBI satellite office"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>There is an <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">FBI</a> satellite office located in Ponce.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>302<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Education">Education</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Arch_at_the_main_entrance_to_the_Pontifical_Catholic_University_of_Puerto_Rico_in_Barrio_Canas_Urbano,_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico_(DSCF0584).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img Rico">Pontifical Catholic University of Puerto Rico</a>, one of over 10 centers of higher learning in the city</figcaption></figure>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Grade_schools_and_high_schools">Grade schools and high schools</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Grade schools and high schools"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Ponce\'s first school for boys was established in 1820.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>303<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Today there are over a hundred public and private schools.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>304<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As with the rest of Puerto Rico, public education in Ponce is handled by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Department_of_Education" title="Puerto Rico Department of Education">Puerto Rico Department of Education</a>. However, the local government is taking on a greater role in public education. On June 13, 2010, the mayor of Ponce announced the creation of a Municipal Education System and a School Board with the objective of obtaining accreditation for what would be the first free bilingual school in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Home_300-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Home-300"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>292<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Colleges_and_universities">Colleges and universities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>There are also several colleges and universities located in the city, offering higher education, including professional degrees in <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">law</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pharmacy" title="Pharmacy">pharmacy</a>. Some of these are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_University" title="Caribbean University">Caribbean University</a> - Ponce</li>\n<li>Colegio Universitario Tecnologico de Ponce<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>305<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Interamerican_University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Ponce" title="Interamerican University of Puerto Rico at Ponce">Interamerican University of Puerto Rico at Ponce</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ponce_School_of_Medicine" class="mw-redirect" title="Ponce School of Medicine">Ponce School of Medicine</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Catholic_University_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Pontifical Catholic University of Puerto Rico">Pontifical Catholic University of Puerto Rico</a>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Catholic_University_of_Puerto_Rico_School_of_Law" title="Pontifical Catholic University of Puerto Rico School of Law">Pontifical Catholic University of Puerto Rico School of Law</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Catholic_University_of_Puerto_Rico_School_of_Architecture" title="Pontifical Catholic University of Puerto Rico School of Architecture">Pontifical Catholic University of Puerto Rico School of Architecture</a></li></ul></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Universidad_Ana_G._M%C3%A9ndez&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Universidad Ana G. M\xc3\xa9ndez (page does not exist)">Universidad Ana G. M\xc3\xa9ndez</a> - Ponce</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Puerto_Rico_at_Ponce" title="University of Puerto Rico at Ponce">University of Puerto Rico at Ponce</a></li></ul>\n<p>There are also several other technical institutions like the <a href="/wiki/Instituto_de_Banca_y_Comercio" title="Instituto de Banca y Comercio">Instituto de Banca y Comercio</a>, Trinity College,<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>306<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the Ponce Paramedical College.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Nova_Southeastern_University" title="Nova Southeastern University">Nova Southeastern University</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lauderdale,_Florida" title="Fort Lauderdale, Florida">Fort Lauderdale, Florida</a>, has a <a href="/wiki/List_of_pharmacy_schools" title="List of pharmacy schools">School of Pharmacy</a> campus in Ponce.<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>307<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Health_care">Health care</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Health care"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The city is served by several clinics and hospitals. There are four comprehensive care hospitals: <a href="/wiki/Hospital_Dr._Pila" class="mw-redirect" title="Hospital Dr. Pila">Hospital Dr. Pila</a>, Hospital San Cristobal, <a href="/wiki/Hospital_San_Lucas" class="mw-redirect" title="Hospital San Lucas">Hospital San Lucas</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>308<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Hospital_de_Damas" class="mw-redirect" title="Hospital de Damas">Hospital de Damas</a>. In addition, <a href="/wiki/Hospital_Oncol%C3%B3gico_Andr%C3%A9s_Grillasca" title="Hospital Oncol\xc3\xb3gico Andr\xc3\xa9s Grillasca">Hospital Oncol\xc3\xb3gico Andr\xc3\xa9s Grillasca</a> specializes in the treatment of cancer,<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>309<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and Hospital Siqui\xc3\xa1trico specializes in mental disorders.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>310<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There is also a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Veterans_Affairs" title="United States Department of Veterans Affairs">U.S. Department of Veterans Affairs</a> Outpatient Clinic that provides health services to U.S. veterans.<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>311<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The U.S. Veterans Administration will build a new hospital in the city to satisfy regional needs.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>312<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2009, Hospital Damas was listed in the <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> as one of the best hospitals under the U.S. flag.<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>313<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\nPonce has the highest concentration of medical infrastructure per inhabitant of any municipality in Puerto Rico.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_roads_in_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="List of roads in Ponce, Puerto Rico">List of roads in Ponce, Puerto Rico</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_streets_in_Ponce,_Puerto_Rico" title="List of streets in Ponce, Puerto Rico">List of streets in Ponce, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>Due to its commercial and industrial significance, Ponce has consistently been a hub of transportation to the rest of the island.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_52" title="Puerto Rico Highway 52">Puerto Rico Highway 52</a> provides access to <a href="/wiki/Salinas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Salinas, Puerto Rico">Salinas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguas, Puerto Rico">Caguas</a>, and San Juan. <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_2" title="Puerto Rico Highway 2">PR-2</a> grants access to southwestern and western municipalities as a full-access freeway. The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_10" title="Puerto Rico Highway 10">PR-10</a> highway, which is still under construction as a faster alternative to <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_123" title="Puerto Rico Highway 123">PR-123</a>, provides access to the interior of the island as well as points north of the island, such as <a href="/wiki/Arecibo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Arecibo, Puerto Rico">Arecibo</a>. <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_1" title="Puerto Rico Highway 1">PR-1</a> provides access to various points east and southeast of Puerto Rico, while <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_14" title="Puerto Rico Highway 14">PR-14</a> provides access to <a href="/wiki/Coamo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Coamo, Puerto Rico">Coamo</a> and other points in the central mountain region. <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_132" title="Puerto Rico Highway 132">PR-132</a> grants country-side access to the town of Pe\xc3\xb1uelas. PR-123 is the old road to Adjuntas and, while treacherous, it does provide an appreciation for countryside living in some of the municipality\'s barrios, such as <a href="/wiki/Magueyes" class="mw-redirect" title="Magueyes">Magueyes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guaraguao" title="Guaraguao">Guaraguao</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>314<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>315<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mercedita_Airport.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Mercedita_Airport.JPG/200px-Mercedita_Airport.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Mercedita_Airport.JPG/300px-Mercedita_Airport.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Mercedita_Airport.JPG/400px-Mercedita_Airport.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a><figcaption>Ponce\'s <a href="/wiki/Mercedita_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercedita Airport">Mercedita Airport</a> used to be an air strip for a sugarcane mill in the early twentieth century</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The city is served by a network of local highways and freeways. Running entirely within the municipal limits are <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_12" title="Puerto Rico Highway 12">PR-12</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_9" title="Puerto Rico Highway 9">PR-9</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_133" title="Puerto Rico Highway 133">PR-133</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_163" title="Puerto Rico Highway 163">PR-163</a> and a few others. Freeway PR-12 runs northbound starting at the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Ponce" class="mw-redirect" title="Port of Ponce">Port of Ponce</a> to connect with <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_14" title="Puerto Rico Highway 14">PR-14</a> on the northeastern part of the city. PR-9, also known as the <i>Circuito de Circumnavegaci\xc3\xb3n de Ponce</i> (Ponce\'s <a href="/wiki/Circumferential_Highway" title="Circumferential Highway">Circumferential Highway</a>), is a highway still partly under construction. It runs mostly north of the city and connects PR-52 to PR-10 in an east-to-west fashion; when completed it will run as a <a href="/wiki/Beltway" class="mw-redirect" title="Beltway">beltway</a> around most of the eastern and northern sections of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>316<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> PR-133 (Calle Comercio) connects PR-2 in west Ponce to PR-132. It is an extension of PR-1 from its PR-2 terminus into the city center. PR-163 crosses the City east-to-west connecting <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_52" title="Puerto Rico Highway 52">PR-52</a> and PR-14.<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>317<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>318<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>319<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>320<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The municipality has 115 bridges.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_329-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-329"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>321<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Ponce\'s public transportation system consists of taxicabs and share taxi service providing <a href="/wiki/Share_taxi" title="Share taxi">public cars and vans</a> known as <i>p\xc3\xbablicos</i><sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>322<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and a bus-based mass transit system.<sup id="cite_ref-elnuevodia.com_331-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elnuevodia.com-331"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>323<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There are five taxi companies in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>324<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Most <i>p\xc3\xbablicos</i> depart from the terminal hub located in downtown Ponce, the <i>Terminal de Carros P\xc3\xbablicos Carlos Garay</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>325<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>326<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During the 1990s and 2000s, there was also a <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">trolley</a> system reminiscent of the one the city used in the 19th century and which traveled through the downtown streets, and which was used mostly by tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>327<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Today it is used mostly during special events. There is also a small train that can bring tourists from the historic downtown area to the <a href="/wiki/Paseo_Tablado_La_Guancha" title="Paseo Tablado La Guancha">Paseo Tablado La Guancha</a> on the southern shore,<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>328<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As with the trolley, today the train is used mostly during special events. A <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferry</a> provides service to <a href="/wiki/Isla_de_Caja_de_Muertos,_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Isla de Caja de Muertos, Puerto Rico">Isla de Caja de Muertos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>329<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The new intra-city mass transit system, <i><a href="/wiki/SITRAS" title="SITRAS">SITRAS</a></i>, was scheduled to start operating in November 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>330<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and, after a 3-month delay, the $4 million SITRAS system, was launched with 11 buses and three routes in February 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-elnuevodia.com_331-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elnuevodia.com-331"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>323<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A fourth route was to be added for the El Tuque sector according to a June 30, 2012 news report.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>331<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mercedita_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercedita Airport">Mercedita Airport</a> sits 3 miles (4.8&#160;km) east of downtown Ponce and handles both intra-island and international flights. The airport, used to be a private airfield belonging to <a href="/wiki/Destiler%C3%ADa_Serralles" class="mw-redirect" title="Destiler\xc3\xada Serralles">Destiler\xc3\xada Serralles</a> rum distillery before it became a commercial airport serving the Ponce area in the 1940s. There is daily commercial non-stop air service to points in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>332<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 1804, Ponce already boasted its own port facilities for large cargo ships.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>333<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Ponce" class="mw-redirect" title="Port of Ponce">Port of Ponce</a> is Puerto Rico\'s chief Caribbean port.<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>334<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is known as the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_the_Americas_(Port_of_Ponce)" class="mw-redirect" title="Port of the Americas (Port of Ponce)">Port of the Americas</a> and is under expansion to convert it into a major international shipping hub.<sup id="cite_ref-ponce.inter.edu_343-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ponce.inter.edu-343"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>335<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It receives both cargo as well as passenger cruise ships.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>336<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>337<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A short-haul freight railroad also operates within the Port facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-PR-chemex_346-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR-chemex-346"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>338<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/PR_primary_14.svg/25px-PR_primary_14.svg.png" decoding="async" width="25" height="25" class="mw-file-element" Rico</a></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="International_relations">International relations</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: International relations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> maintains a consular office in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>339<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Twin_towns_\xe2\x80\x93_sister_cities"><span id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities"></span>Twin towns \xe2\x80\x93 sister cities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Twin towns \xe2\x80\x93 sister cities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Ponce is <a href="/wiki/Sister_city" title="Sister city">twinned</a> with:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><span class="mw-image-border" typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain"><img alt="Spain" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/23px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/35px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Spain.svg/45px-Flag_of_Spain.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="500" /></a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Zaragoza" title="Zaragoza">Zaragoza</a>, Spain<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>340<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Commemorative_dates">Commemorative dates</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Commemorative dates"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The following dates hold special significance for Ponce\xc3\xb1os and are motive for annual celebrations and/or memorials:\n</p>\n<ul><li><u>January 25:</u> <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_town_and_city_fires#1890s" title="List of town and city fires">El Polvor\xc3\xadn fire</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>341<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Often remembered with a service at the <a href="/wiki/Monumento_a_los_heroes_de_El_Polvor%C3%ADn_(mausoleum)" class="mw-redirect" title="Monumento a los heroes de El Polvor\xc3\xadn (mausoleum)">mausoleum of the Ponce firefighters</a> at <a href="/wiki/Cementerio_Civil_de_Ponce" title="Cementerio Civil de Ponce">Cementerio Civil de Ponce</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>342<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><u>March 21:</u> <i><a href="/wiki/Ponce_massacre" title="Ponce massacre">Ponce massacre</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>343<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Often memorialized with a get-together and service at the tomb of the victims at <a href="/wiki/Cementerio_Civil_de_Ponce" title="Cementerio Civil de Ponce">Cementerio Civil de Ponce</a><sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>344<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><u>March 22:</u> <i>Abolition of slavery in Puerto Rico.</i><sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>345<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Often remembered with a <a href="/wiki/Funeral#Memorial_services" title="Funeral">memorial service</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Monumento_a_la_abolici%C3%B3n_de_la_esclavitud" title="Monumento a la abolici\xc3\xb3n de la esclavitud">Monumento a la abolici\xc3\xb3n de la esclavitud</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>346<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><u>April 26 (or, last Sunday of April):</u> <i>D\xc3\xada de la Bandera Ponce\xc3\xb1a.</i><sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>347<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><u>August 12:</u> <i><a href="/wiki/D%C3%ADa_Mundial_de_Ponce" title="D\xc3\xada Mundial de Ponce">D\xc3\xada de la Fundaci\xc3\xb3n de Ponce (Founding Date)</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-Mariano_Vidal_Armstrong_1986._p._17_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mariano_Vidal_Armstrong_1986._p._17-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>348<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>349<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Often celebrated on the first Sunday of September.<sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>350<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><u>October 7:</u> <i><a href="/wiki/Mameyes_Landslide" class="mw-redirect" title="Mameyes Landslide">Mameyes Landslide</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>351<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>352<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>353<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Often remembered with a get-together and memorial service at the site of the landslide in <a href="/wiki/Barrio_Portugu%C3%A9s_Urbano" class="mw-redirect" title="Barrio Portugu\xc3\xa9s Urbano">Barrio Portugu\xc3\xa9s Urbano</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>354<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><u>December 12:</u> <i><a href="/wiki/Las_Ma%C3%B1anitas_(celebration)" title="Las Ma\xc3\xb1anitas (celebration)">Las Ma\xc3\xb1anitas</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>355<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Celebrated yearly with a pre-dawn festival parade, followed by a Catholic <a href="/wiki/Mass_(Catholic_Church)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mass (Catholic Church)">Mass</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/People" title="People">popular</a> town breakfast.<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>356<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="See_also">See also</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
