class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notes">Notes</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Notes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1239543626">.mw-parser-output .reflist{margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}@media screen{.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%}}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-27">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Some publications/reporters have erroneously stated Ponce\'s date of founding as December 12, 1692 (see, for example, Jose Fernandez-Colon, The Associated Press, at "Noticias Online" on January 24, 2009, at <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20150202012710/http://www.noticiasonline.com/Det.asp?id=17952"><i>Noticias Puerto Rico.</i></a> Accessed 23 March 2019.) Another incorrect date sometimes found is September 12, 1692 (See, for example, Jorge L. Perez (El Nuevo Dia) and Jorge Figueroa (Ponce Municipal Historian), at <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.prhbds.org/ponce/"><i>Historic Buildings and Structures in Ponce, Puerto Rico.</i></a>, at the text accompanying Drawing #20, titled "Tumba de los Bomberos". Puerto Rico Historic Buildings Drawings Society. 2019. Accessed 4 February 2019. See also <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://demografia.rcm.upr.edu/images/Memorias_municipios/Memoria_27_Ponce-1953.pdf"><i>Mapa de Municipios y Barrios: Ponce, Memoria Numero 27.</i></a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20190430032312/http://demografia.rcm.upr.edu/images/Memorias_municipios/Memoria_27_Ponce-1953.pdf">Archived</a> 30 April 2019 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a> Gobierno del Estado Libre Asociado de Puerto Rico. Junta de Planificaci\xc3\xb3n. Santurce, Puerto Rico. 1953. p. 6.). Miguel A Sanchez-Celada also points to the September 12, 1692 date based on the record that on that date the Spanish Crown officially recognized, via Royal Decree, the hamlet as a town (See Miguel A Sanchez-Celada. <i>Evoluci\xc3\xb3n urbana de Ponce (Puerto_Rico) seg\xc3\xban la cartograf\xc3\xada Hist\xc3\xb3rica.</i> Universidad Nacional de Educaci\xc3\xb3n a Distancia (UNED), Madrid, Spain. 2018. (DOI:http:..dx.doi.org/10.5944/etfvi.11.2018.20421) In, Espacio, Tiempo y Forma", Revista de la Facultad de Geografia e Historia, UNED. Serie VI. Geograf\xc3\xada 11. 2018, pp. 219-245. ISSN 1130-2968. E-ISSN 2340-146x.) In this article the date reported is that given by the authorities closest to the founding date, and with their respective references.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Some historians state that the municipality was named after Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n himself. (Crediting Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n himself see, for example, Eduardo Neuman Gandia\'s <i>Verdadera y Aut\xc3\xa9ntica Historia de la Ciudad de Ponce.</i> (San Juan, Puerto Rico: Instituto de Cultura Puertorrique\xc3\xb1a. 1913.) Page 34, and Jose Luis Diaz de Villegas, <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=ovzJlU1f-iAC&amp;pg=PA46">https://books.google.com/books?id=ovzJlU1f-iAC&amp;pg=PA46</a>, and Sandra Torres Guzm\xc3\xa1n\'s <i> Una hacienda atada a la historia citadina</i>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://www.periodicolaperla.com/una-hacienda-atada-a-la-historia-citadina/">https://www.periodicolaperla.com/una-hacienda-atada-a-la-historia-citadina/</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20190925123950/https://www.periodicolaperla.com/una-hacienda-atada-a-la-historia-citadina/">Archived</a> 25 September 2019 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>.) Others state it was named after Juan Ponce de Leon y Loayza, the great-grandson of Juan Ponce de Leon. (Crediting the great-grandson see, for example, Encyclopedia Puerto Rico, <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1238218222"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20120529141914/http://www.enciclopediapr.org/ing/article.cfm?ref=09012901&amp;page=2">"Municipalities: Ponce"</a>. Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.enciclopediapr.org/ing/article.cfm?ref=09012901&amp;page=2">the original</a> on 29 May 2012<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">25 July</span> 2012</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Municipalities%3A+Ponce&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.enciclopediapr.org%2Fing%2Farticle.cfm%3Fref%3D09012901%26page%3D2&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APonce%2C+Puerto+Rico" class="Z3988"></span>; J.A. Corretjer, <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.yerbabruja.com/pueblos/ponce.html">http://www.yerbabruja.com/pueblos/ponce.html</a>; Frommer, <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Wy_BSu4a2EYC&amp;pg=PA185">https://books.google.com/books?id=Wy_BSu4a2EYC&amp;pg=PA185</a>; and Harry S. Pariser, <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=KawuqbFxLS0C&amp;pg=PT239">https://books.google.com/books?id=KawuqbFxLS0C&amp;pg=PT239</a>.) A few authorities state it may have been named after the Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n family in general, covering father, son, grandson, and great-grandson (See, for example, Francisco Lluch Mora\'s <i>"Or\xc3\xadgenes y Fundaci\xc3\xb3n de Ponce, y otras noticias relativas a su desarrollo urbano, demogr\xc3\xa1fico y cultural (siglos XVI-XIX)"</i>, Segunda Edici\xc3\xb3n, Editorial Plaza Mayor, 2006, page 27.). Still others state it was founded by Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n y Loayza but <u>named by him</u> in the memory of his great-grandfather, the Spanish Conquistador Juan Ponce de Le\xc3\xb3n.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Footnotes">Footnotes</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Footnotes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1239543626"><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">During the 1600s and 1700s, the rural areas of a municipal jurisdiction, today (2019) called "<a href="/wiki/Barrio" title="Barrio">barrio</a>" in Puerto Rico, were then called "partido", a term used to refer to all the territory that depended from the Municipal Government of a city or town (See, Lorenzo A. Balasquide, <i>Compendio Intrahist\xc3\xb3rico de Pe\xc3\xb1uelas</i>, San Juan, Puerto Rico: Editorial Cordillera, Inc., 1972, p. 51, footnote #23; Aida R. Caro Costas, <i>El Cabildo or Regimen Municipal Puertorrique\xc3\xb1o en el Siglo XVIII: La Gesti\xc3\xb3n Municipal Puertorrique\xc3\xb1a</i>, Tomo II, San Juan, Puerto Rico: Instituto de Cultura Puertorrique\xc3\xb1a, 1974, p. 38). In 1670, that Municipal Government was <a href="/wiki/San_Germ%C3%A1n,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Germ\xc3\xa1n, Puerto Rico">San Germ\xc3\xa1n</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-32">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Coined "Ciudad Se\xc3\xb1orial" by <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Fern%C3%A1ndez_Juncos" title="Manuel Fern\xc3\xa1ndez Juncos">Manuel Fern\xc3\xa1ndez Juncos</a> in 1864 upon the inauguration of <a href="/wiki/Teatro_La_Perla" title="Teatro La Perla">Teatro La Perla</a>. (Ref: Neysa Rodriguez Deynes, Rafael J. Torres Torres, and Carlos Aneiro Perez. "Teatro La Perla", in <i>Brevario Sobre la Historia de Ponce y Sus Principales Lugares de Inter\xc3\xa9s.</i> Gobierno Municipal de Ponce (Ponce, Puerto Rico). Model Offset Printing. 1991. page 125.)</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-33">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sometimes also translated "The Patrician City" (See, Ileana M. Rodr\xc3\xadguez-Silva\'s "Silencing Race: Disentangling Blackness, Colonialism, and National Identities in Puerto Rico". New York: Basingstoke, Palgrave Macmillan. 2012. Page 94.) or "The Noble City" (See <i>Ponce: General Information.</i> Puerto Rico Encyclopedia. Retrieved 25 November 2009.), but translations into "The Majestic City" (See Fundaci\xc3\xb3n Puertorrique\xc3\xb1a de las Humanidades. <i>Ponce Ciudad Museo 2001.</i> 2001. p. 149.), "The Lordly City" (See <i>La Perla Theater in Ponce</i>. Ivonne Acosta. Encyclopedia de Puerto Rico. 29 September 2008. Accessed 28 November 2018.), and "The Estately City", have also been encountered.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-185"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-185">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For an extensive discussion of the Plan Ponce en Marcha, see Carmelo Rosario Natal, "Ponce en Marcha y las Primeras Iniciativas", in <i>"Ponce en Su Historia Moderna: 1945-2002,"</i> Gobierno Municipal de Ponce, First Edition, 2003, Pages 242-324.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-225"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-225">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">It has, also, been called a "more profoundly Puerto Rican city than San Juan". See Enrique A. Laguerre\'s "Mito de la ponce\xc3\xb1idad", <i><a href="/wiki/El_Mundo_(Puerto_Rico)" title="El Mundo (Puerto Rico)">El Mundo</a></i>, 8 November 1980, page 9-A.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-275"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-275">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Ayuntamiento de Ponce</i> was the second formed in Puerto Rico, after San Juan\'s. See <i>Historia de los partidos reformista y conservador de Puerto-Rico.</i> Francisco Mariano Qui\xc3\xb1ones. Tipograf\xc3\xada Comercial Comercio 13, Marina. Mayaguez, Puerto Rico. 1889. Page 7.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="References">References</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ponce,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: References"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1239543626"><div class="reflist">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Fay Fowlie de Flores. <i>Ponce, Perla del Sur: Una Bibliogr\xc3\xa1fica Anotada.</i> Second Edition. 1997.
